<p><b>Bermuda</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/ər/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">ər</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/j/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;yes&#39;">j</span><span title="/uː/: &#39;oo&#39; in &#39;goose&#39;">uː</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>) (in full, the <i>Islands of Bermuda</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a> in the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Ocean" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic Ocean</a>. It is approximately 1,070&#160;km (665&#160;mi) east-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras" title="Cape Hatteras">Cape Hatteras</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>; 1,236&#160;km (768&#160;mi) south of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Sable_Island" title="Cape Sable Island">Cape Sable Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>; and 1,759&#160;km (1,093&#160;mi) northeast of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital city</a> is <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Bermuda" title="Hamilton, Bermuda">Hamilton</a>. Bermuda is self-governing, with its own constitution and government and a Parliament which makes local laws. The United Kingdom retains responsibility for defence and foreign relations. As of July 2018, it has a population of 71,176, making it the most populous of the British overseas territories.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bermuda's two largest <a href="/wiki/Economic_sector" title="Economic sector">economic sectors</a> are offshore <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">insurance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reinsurance" title="Reinsurance">reinsurance</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Smithsonian_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smithsonian-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Bermuda had one of the world's highest <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> for most of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> It has a <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">subtropical</a> climate<sup id="cite_ref-climate_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and lies in the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_belt" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane belt">hurricane belt</a> and thus is prone to related severe weather; however, it is somewhat protected by a coral reef that surrounds the island and its position at the north of the belt, which limits the direction and severity of approaching storms.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bermuda is named after the Spanish sailor <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Berm%C3%BAdez" title="Juan de Bermúdez">Juan de Bermúdez</a>, who discovered the islands in 1505.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bermuda" title="History of Bermuda">History of Bermuda</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery">Discovery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Discovery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Bermuda_1511_legatio_babylonica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Map_of_Bermuda_1511_legatio_babylonica.jpg/280px-Map_of_Bermuda_1511_legatio_babylonica.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Map_of_Bermuda_1511_legatio_babylonica.jpg/420px-Map_of_Bermuda_1511_legatio_babylonica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/34/Map_of_Bermuda_1511_legatio_babylonica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="496" data-file-height="320" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Bermuda_1511_legatio_babylonica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>First map of the island of Bermuda in 1511, made by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Martyr_d%27Anghiera" title="Peter Martyr d&#39;Anghiera">Peter Martyr d'Anghiera</a> in his book <i>Legatio Babylonica</i></div></div></div>
<p>Bermuda was discovered in 1505 by Spanish explorer <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Berm%C3%BAdez" title="Juan de Bermúdez">Juan de Bermúdez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Morison1974_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morison1974-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Bermuda had no indigenous population at the time of its discovery, nor at the time of the initial British settlement a century later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGovern201810_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGovern201810-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It was mentioned in <i>Legatio Babylonica</i>, published in 1511 by historian <a href="/wiki/Pedro_M%C3%A1rtir" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedro Mártir">Pedro Mártir de Anglería</a>, and was also included on Spanish charts of that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Frommers_-_History_of_Bermuda_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frommers_-_History_of_Bermuda-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Both Spanish and Portuguese ships used the islands as a replenishment spot to take on fresh meat and water; for example, shipwrecked Portuguese mariners are now thought to have been responsible for the 1543 inscription on <a href="/wiki/Spittal_Pond_Nature_Reserve" title="Spittal Pond Nature Reserve">Portuguese Rock</a> (previously called Spanish Rock).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Legends arose of <a href="/wiki/Spirit" title="Spirit">spirits</a> and devils, now thought to have stemmed from the calls of raucous birds (most likely the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_petrel" title="Bermuda petrel">Bermuda petrel</a>, or <i>cahow</i>) and the loud noise heard at night from wild hogs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Combined with the frequent storm-wracked conditions and the dangerous reefs, the archipelago became known as the 'Isle of Devils'.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Neither Spain nor Portugal attempted to settle it.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement_by_the_English">Settlement by the English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Settlement by the English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Generall_Historie_of_Virginia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Generall_Historie_of_Virginia.jpg/220px-Generall_Historie_of_Virginia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="335" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Generall_Historie_of_Virginia.jpg/330px-Generall_Historie_of_Virginia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Generall_Historie_of_Virginia.jpg/440px-Generall_Historie_of_Virginia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="651" data-file-height="992" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Generall_Historie_of_Virginia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Smith_(explorer)" title="John Smith (explorer)">John Smith</a> wrote one of the first <a href="/wiki/The_Generall_Historie_of_Virginia,_New-England,_and_the_Summer_Isles" title="The Generall Historie of Virginia, New-England, and the Summer Isles">histories of Bermuda</a> in 1624 (combined with <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>).</div></div></div>
<p>For the next century, the island is believed to have been visited frequently, but not settled. The English had by this time started to take an interest in the 'New' World, initially attempting to settle in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> in what is now the eastern United States. After the failure of the first two English colonies here, a more determined effort was initiated by King <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="James I of England">James I of England</a>, who granted a Royal Charter to the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Company" title="Virginia Company">Virginia Company</a> which established a colony at <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">Jamestown, Virginia</a> in 1607. Two years later, a <a href="/wiki/Flotilla" title="Flotilla">flotilla</a> of seven ships left England under the company's admiral, Sir <a href="/wiki/George_Somers" title="George Somers">George Somers</a>, and the new governor of Jamestown, Sir <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Gates_(governor)" title="Thomas Gates (governor)">Thomas Gates</a>, with several hundred settlers, food and supplies to relieve the colony of Jamestown.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> However the flotilla was broken up by a storm; as the <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_Venture" title="Sea Venture"><i>Sea Venture</i></a>, was taking on water, Somers drove it onto Bermuda's reef and reached the shores safely with smaller boats – all 150 passengers and a dog survived.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>(<a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">William Shakespeare</a>'s play <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tempest_(play)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Tempest (play)">The Tempest</a></i>, in which the character <a href="/wiki/Ariel_(The_Tempest)" title="Ariel (The Tempest)">Ariel</a> refers to the "still-vex'd Bermoothes" (I.ii.229), is thought to have been inspired by <a href="/wiki/William_Strachey" title="William Strachey">William Strachey</a>'s account of this shipwreck.)<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> They stayed 10 months, starting a new settlement and building two small ships, the Deliverance and the Patience, to sail on to Jamestown. Bermuda was claimed for the English Crown, and the charter of the Virginia Company was later extended to include them.
</p><p>On 10 May 1610, all but two of the remaining survivors of <i>Sea Venture</i> sailed on to Jamestown (excluding those who had died or been killed on Bermuda, or the crew of the Sea Venture's longboat, sent under Henry Ravens to Virginia a month after the wreck of the Sea Venture, none of whom were seen again; but including children born in Bermuda). Among them was <a href="/wiki/John_Rolfe" title="John Rolfe">John Rolfe</a>, whose wife and child died and were buried in Bermuda. Somers returned to Bermuda with the Plough to obtain food for the starving settlers of Jamestown but died in Bermuda; the Plough sailed instead for England, leaving a third man with the two who had remained behind in May. In 1612, the English began the intentional settlement of the archipelago, officially named <i>Virgineola</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> with the arrival of the ship the <i>Plough</i>. <i>New London</i> (soon renamed St. George's Town) was settled that year and designated as the colony's first capital.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Frommers_-_History_of_Bermuda_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frommers_-_History_of_Bermuda-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> It is the oldest continually inhabited English town in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Smithsonian_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smithsonian-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1615, the colony, which had been renamed the Somers Isles in commemoration of Sir George Somers, was passed to a new company, the <a href="/wiki/Somers_Isles_Company" title="Somers Isles Company">Somers Isles Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> As Bermudians settled <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Colony" class="mw-redirect" title="Carolina Colony">Carolina Colony</a> and contributed to the establishment of other English colonies in the Americas, <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Bermuda (disambiguation)">many other locations were also named after the archipelago</a>. During this period the first slaves were brought to the islands. These were a mixture of African and Native American slaves, shipwreck victims from enemy nations, and political prisoners from Scotland and Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The archipelago's limited land area and resources led to the creation of what may be the earliest conservation laws of the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>. In 1616 and 1620 acts were passed banning the hunting of certain <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a> and young <a href="/wiki/Tortoise" title="Tortoise">tortoises</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">Civil War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Civil War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1649, the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a> was in its seventh year and King <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a> was beheaded in <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Whitehall" title="Palace of Whitehall">Whitehall</a>, London. The conflict spilled over into Bermuda, where the majority of the colonists developed a strong sense of devotion to the Crown. Bermuda's civil war was ended by militias, and dissenters such as <a href="/wiki/Puritan" class="mw-redirect" title="Puritan">Puritans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independent_(religion)" title="Independent (religion)">Independents</a> were pushed to settle <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a> under <a href="/wiki/William_Sayle" title="William Sayle">William Sayle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The rebellious Royalist colonies of Bermuda and Virginia, as well as <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>, were the subjects of <a href="/wiki/An_Act_for_prohibiting_Trade_with_the_Barbadoes,_Virginia,_Bermuda_and_Antego" title="An Act for prohibiting Trade with the Barbadoes, Virginia, Bermuda and Antego">an Act of the Rump Parliament of England</a>, which was essentially a declaration of war. The Act, prohibiting Trade with Barbados, Virginia, Bermuda and Antigua, specified that:<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>due punishment [be] inflicted upon the said Delinquents, do Declare all and every the said persons in Barbada's, Antego, Bermuda's and Virginia, that have contrived, abetted, aided or assisted those horrid Rebellions, or have since willingly joyned with them, to be notorious Robbers and Traitors, and such as by the Law of Nations are not to be permitted any maner of Commerce or Traffique with any people whatsoever; and do forbid to all maner of persons, Foreiners, and others, all maner of Commerce, Traffique and Correspondency whatsoever, to be used or held with the said Rebels in the Barbada's, Bermuda's, Virginia and Antego, or either of them.
</p><p>All Ships that Trade with the Rebels may be surprized. Goods and tackle of such ships not to be embezeled, till judgement in the Admiralty.; Two or three of the Officers of every ship to be examined upon oath.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>The Royalist colonies were also threatened with invasion. The Government of Bermuda eventually reached an agreement with the Parliamentarians in England which left the status quo in Bermuda.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_17th_century">Later 17th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Later 17th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_Gazette_-_12_November_1796.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Bermuda_Gazette_-_12_November_1796.jpg/220px-Bermuda_Gazette_-_12_November_1796.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="312" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Bermuda_Gazette_-_12_November_1796.jpg/330px-Bermuda_Gazette_-_12_November_1796.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/Bermuda_Gazette_-_12_November_1796.jpg/440px-Bermuda_Gazette_-_12_November_1796.jpg 2x" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="817" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_Gazette_-_12_November_1796.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Bermuda Gazette</i> of 12 November 1796, calling for <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateering</a> against Spain and its allies; it has advertisements for crew for two privateer vessels.</div></div></div>
<p>In the 17th century, the Somers Isles Company suppressed shipbuilding, as it needed Bermudians to farm in order for it to generate income from the land. The colony of Virginia far surpassed Bermuda in both quality and quantity of <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a> produced. Bermudians began to turn to maritime trades relatively early in the 17th century, but the Somers Isles Company used all its authority to suppress turning away from agriculture. This interference led to the islanders demanding, and receiving, the revocation of the company's charter in 1684, and the company was dissolved.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bermudians rapidly abandoned agriculture for shipbuilding, replanting farmland with the native juniper (<i><a href="/wiki/Juniperus_bermudiana" title="Juniperus bermudiana">Juniperus bermudiana</a></i>, called <i>Bermuda cedar</i>) trees that grew thickly over the entire island. Establishing effective control over the <a href="/wiki/Turks_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Turks Islands">Turks Islands</a>, Bermudians deforested their landscape to begin the salt trade. It became the world's largest and remained the cornerstone of Bermuda's economy for the next century. Bermudians also vigorously pursued <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Privateering" class="mw-redirect" title="Privateering">privateering</a>, and the merchant trade.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_sloop" title="Bermuda sloop">Bermuda sloop</a> became highly regarded for its speed and manoeuvrability, and was soon adapted for service with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>. The Bermuda sloop <a href="/wiki/HMS_Pickle_(1800)" title="HMS Pickle (1800)">HMS&#160;<i>Pickle</i></a> carried dispatches of the victory at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Trafalgar</a>, and news of the death of <a href="/wiki/Admiral_Lord_Nelson" class="mw-redirect" title="Admiral Lord Nelson">Admiral Nelson</a>, to England.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bermuda_and_the_American_War_of_Independence">Bermuda and the American War of Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Bermuda and the American War of Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bermuda's ambivalence towards the American rebellion changed in September 1774, when the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">Continental Congress</a> resolved to ban trade with Great Britain, Ireland, and the West Indies after 10 September 1775. Such an embargo would mean the collapse of their intercolonial commerce, famine and civil unrest. Lacking political channels with Great Britain, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Tucker_(President_of_the_Council_of_Bermuda)" title="Henry Tucker (President of the Council of Bermuda)">the Tucker Family</a> met in May 1775 with eight other parishioners, and resolved to send delegates to the Continental Congress in July, with the goal of an exemption from the ban. Henry Tucker noted a clause in the ban which allowed the exchange of American goods for military supplies. The clause was confirmed by <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">Benjamin Franklin</a> when Tucker met with the Pennsylvania <a href="/wiki/Committees_of_safety_(American_Revolution)" title="Committees of safety (American Revolution)">Committee of Safety</a>. Independently, Tucker's sons St. George and Thomas Tudor confirmed this business arrangement with <a href="/wiki/Peyton_Randolph" title="Peyton Randolph">Peyton Randolph</a> and the Charlestown Committee of Safety, while another Bermudian, Harris, did so with <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jarvis_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarvis-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Three American vessels, independently operating from Charlestown, Philadelphia and Newport, sailed to Bermuda, and on 14 August 1775, 100 barrels of gunpowder were taken from the Bermudian magazine, while Governor <a href="/wiki/George_James_Bruere" title="George James Bruere">George James Bruere</a> slept, and loaded onto these vessels. As a consequence, on 2 October the Continental Congress exempted Bermuda from their trade ban, and Bermuda acquired a reputation for disloyalty. Later that year, the British Parliament passed the <a href="/wiki/Prohibitory_Act" title="Prohibitory Act">Prohibitory Act</a> to prohibit trade with the American rebelling colonies, and sent HMS <i>Scorpion</i> to keep watch over the island. The island's forts were stripped of cannon, such that by the end of 1775, all of Bermuda's forts were without cannon, shot and powder. Yet, wartime trade of contraband continued along well established family connections. With 120 vessels by 1775, Bermuda continued to trade with <a href="/wiki/St._Eustatius" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Eustatius">St. Eustatius</a> until 1781, and provided salt to North American ports, despite the presence of hundreds of privateers.<sup id="cite_ref-Jarvis_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarvis-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>389–415</span></sup>
</p><p>In June 1776, HMS <i>Nautilus</i> secured the island, followed by <a href="/wiki/HMS_Galatea_(1776)" title="HMS Galatea (1776)">HMS&#160;<i>Galatea</i></a> in September. Yet, the two British captains seemed more intent on capturing prize money, causing a severe food shortage on the island until the departure of <i>Nautilus</i> in October. After France's entry into the war in 1778, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Clinton_(British_Army_officer,_born_1730)" title="Henry Clinton (British Army officer, born 1730)">Sir Henry Clinton</a> refortified and garrisoned the island under the command of Major <a href="/wiki/William_Sutherland_(British_Army_officer)" title="William Sutherland (British Army officer)">William Sutherland</a>. As a result, 91 French and American ships were captured in the winter of 1778–1779, bringing the population once again to the brink of starvation. Bermudian trade was severely hampered by the combined efforts of the Royal Navy, the British garrison and <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">loyalist privateers</a>, such that famine struck the island in 1779.<sup id="cite_ref-Jarvis_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarvis-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>416–427</span></sup>
</p><p>The death of George Bruere in 1780 turned the governorship over to his son, George Jr., an active loyalist. Under his leadership, smuggling was stopped, and the Bermudian colonial government populated with like-minded loyalists. Even Henry Tucker abandoned trading with the United States, because of the presence of many privateers. Loyalist privateers based in Bermuda captured 114 prizes between 1777 and 1781, while 130 were captured in 1782.<sup id="cite_ref-Jarvis_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarvis-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>428–433</span></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/The_Bermuda_Gazette" title="The Bermuda Gazette">The Bermuda Gazette</a>, Bermuda's first newspaper, began publishing in 1784.<sup id="cite_ref-Stark_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stark-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200th_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200th-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TBG_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TBG-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Devonshire_Redoubt_(Bermuda).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Devonshire_Redoubt_%28Bermuda%29.png/220px-Devonshire_Redoubt_%28Bermuda%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/90/Devonshire_Redoubt_%28Bermuda%29.png 1.5x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="286" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Devonshire_Redoubt_(Bermuda).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An illustration of the Devonshire Redoubt, Bermuda, 1614</div></div></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> began improving the harbours on the Bermudas. In 1811, work began on the large <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Dockyard,_Bermuda" title="Royal Naval Dockyard, Bermuda">Royal Naval Dockyard</a> on <a href="/wiki/Ireland_Island,_Bermuda" title="Ireland Island, Bermuda">Ireland Island</a>, in the west of the chain, which was to serve as the islands' principal naval base guarding the western Atlantic Ocean shipping lanes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> To guard the dockyard, the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> built a large <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Garrison" title="Bermuda Garrison">Bermuda Garrison</a>, and heavily fortified the archipelago.
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> between Britain and the United States, the <a href="/wiki/Burning_of_Washington" title="Burning of Washington">British attacks</a> on <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake</a> were planned and launched from Bermuda, where the headquarters of the Royal Navy's <a href="/wiki/North_America_and_West_Indies_Station" title="North America and West Indies Station">North American Station</a> had recently been moved from <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax, Nova Scotia">Halifax, Nova Scotia</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Harbor_at_St._George,_Bermuda_from_Sugar_Loaf_Hill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/The_Harbor_at_St._George%2C_Bermuda_from_Sugar_Loaf_Hill.jpg/220px-The_Harbor_at_St._George%2C_Bermuda_from_Sugar_Loaf_Hill.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/The_Harbor_at_St._George%2C_Bermuda_from_Sugar_Loaf_Hill.jpg/330px-The_Harbor_at_St._George%2C_Bermuda_from_Sugar_Loaf_Hill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/The_Harbor_at_St._George%2C_Bermuda_from_Sugar_Loaf_Hill.jpg/440px-The_Harbor_at_St._George%2C_Bermuda_from_Sugar_Loaf_Hill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5727" data-file-height="3656" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Harbor_at_St._George,_Bermuda_from_Sugar_Loaf_Hill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The harbour at <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Bermuda" title="St. George&#39;s, Bermuda">St. George's</a>, the original capital.</div></div></div><p>In 1816, James Arnold, the son of <a href="/wiki/Benedict_Arnold" title="Benedict Arnold">Benedict Arnold</a>, fortified Bermuda's Royal Naval Dockyard against possible US attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Today, the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Bermuda" title="National Museum of Bermuda">National Museum of Bermuda</a>, which incorporates Bermuda's Maritime Museum, occupies the <a href="/wiki/Keep" title="Keep">Keep</a> of the Royal Naval Dockyard, including the Commissioner's House, and exhibits artifacts of the base's military history.
</p><p>The British <a href="/wiki/Slave_Trade_Act_1807" title="Slave Trade Act 1807">abolished the slave trade</a> in 1807, but not the institution itself.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> As a result of frequent slave rebellions in their other colonies, as well as the efforts of abolitionists, the British outlawed slavery in its empire in 1834.<sup id="cite_ref-Frommers_-_History_of_Bermuda_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frommers_-_History_of_Bermuda-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to its proximity to the southeastern US coast, Bermuda was frequently used during the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> as a stopping point base for the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Confederate States">Confederate States</a>' <a href="/wiki/Blockade_runners_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Blockade runners of the American Civil War">blockade runners</a> on their runs to and from the Southern states, and England, to evade Union naval vessels on blockade patrol;<sup id="cite_ref-Frommers_-_History_of_Bermuda_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frommers_-_History_of_Bermuda-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> the blockade runners were then able to transport essential war goods from England and deliver much needed cotton back to England. The old Globe Hotel in St George's, which was a centre of intrigue for Confederate agents, is preserved as a public museum.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Anglo-Boer_War">Anglo-Boer War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Anglo-Boer War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Boer_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Boer War">Anglo-Boer War</a> (1899–1902), 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Boer" title="Boer">Boer</a> <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners of war</a> were housed on five islands of Bermuda. They were located according to their views of the war. "Bitterenders" (Afrikaans: <a href="/wiki/Bittereinder" title="Bittereinder">Bittereinders</a>), who refused to pledge allegiance to the British Crown, were interned on Darrell's Island and closely guarded. Other islands such as Morgan's Island held 884 men, including 27 officers; Tucker's Island held 809 Boer prisoners, Burt's Island 607, and Port's Island held 35.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported an attempted mutiny by Boer prisoners of war en route to Bermuda and that martial law was enacted on Darrell's Island,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> in addition to the escape of three Boer prisoners to mainland Bermuda,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> a young Boer soldier stowed away and sailed from Bermuda to New York on the steamship <i>Trinidad</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most famous escapee was the Boer prisoner of war Captain <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Joubert_Duquesne" title="Fritz Joubert Duquesne">Fritz Joubert Duquesne</a>, who was serving a life sentence for "conspiracy against the British government and on (the charge of) espionage".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERonnie199537_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERonnie199537-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On the night of 25 June 1902, Duquesne slipped out of his tent, worked his way over a barbed-wire fence, swam 1.5 miles (2.4&#160;km) past patrol boats and bright spot lights, through storm-wracked waters, using the distant <a href="/wiki/Gibbs_Hill_Lighthouse" title="Gibbs Hill Lighthouse">Gibbs Hill Lighthouse</a> for navigation until he arrived ashore on the main island.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERonnie199554,63_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERonnie199554,63-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> From there he escaped to the port of <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Bermuda" title="St. George&#39;s, Bermuda">St. George's</a> and a week later, he stowed away on a boat heading to Baltimore, Maryland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERonnie199565–66_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERonnie199565–66-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He settled in the US and later became a spy for Germany in both World Wars. He claimed to be responsible for the 1916 death of <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Herbert_Kitchener,_1st_Earl_Kitchener" class="mw-redirect" title="Horatio Herbert Kitchener, 1st Earl Kitchener">Lord Kitchener</a> in the sinking of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Hampshire_(1903)" title="HMS Hampshire (1903)">HMS&#160;<i>Hampshire</i></a>, the head of the British Army who had also commanded British forces in South Africa during the second Boer War, but this had resulted from a mine. In 1942, Col. Duquesne was arrested by the <a href="/wiki/FBI" class="mw-redirect" title="FBI">FBI</a> for leading the <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_Spy_Ring" title="Duquesne Spy Ring">Duquesne Spy Ring</a>, which still to this day is the largest espionage case in the history of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDuffy20142_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDuffy20142-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lord Kitchener's brother, Lt. Gen. Sir <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Walter_Kitchener" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick Walter Kitchener">Walter Kitchener</a>, had been the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Bermuda" title="Governor of Bermuda">governor of Bermuda</a> from 1908 until his death in 1912. His son, Major Hal Kitchener, bought <a href="/wiki/Hinson%27s_Island,_Bermuda" title="Hinson&#39;s Island, Bermuda">Hinson's Island</a> (with his partner, Major Hemming, another First World War aviator). The island had formerly been part of the Boer POW camp, housing teenaged prisoners from 1901 to 1902.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_and_21st_centuries">20th and 21st centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 20th and 21st centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_harbour_1926.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bermuda_harbour_1926.jpg/220px-Bermuda_harbour_1926.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bermuda_harbour_1926.jpg/330px-Bermuda_harbour_1926.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bermuda_harbour_1926.jpg/440px-Bermuda_harbour_1926.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1311" data-file-height="764" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_harbour_1926.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Harbour,_Bermuda" title="Hamilton Harbour, Bermuda">Hamilton Harbour</a> in the mid-1920s.</div></div></div>
<p>In the early 20th century, as modern transport and communication systems developed, Bermuda became a popular destination for American, Canadian and British tourists arriving by sea. The United States <a href="/wiki/Smoot%E2%80%93Hawley_Tariff_Act" title="Smoot–Hawley Tariff Act">Smoot–Hawley Tariff Act</a> of 1930, which enacted protectionist trade <a href="/wiki/Tariffs" class="mw-redirect" title="Tariffs">tariffs</a> on goods imported into the US, led to the demise of Bermuda's once-thriving agricultural export trade to America and encouraged the development of tourism as an alternative source of income. The island was one of the centres for illegal alcohol smuggling during the era of <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">Prohibition in the United States</a> (1920-1933).<sup id="cite_ref-Frommers_-_History_of_Bermuda_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frommers_-_History_of_Bermuda-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda_9-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1930, after several failed attempts, a <a href="/wiki/Stinson_Detroiter" title="Stinson Detroiter">Stinson Detroiter</a> <a href="/wiki/Seaplane" title="Seaplane">seaplane</a> flew to Bermuda from <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, the first aeroplane ever to reach the islands. The flight was not without incident, as the aircraft had to land twice in the ocean, once because of darkness and again when it needed to refuel.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Navigation and weather forecasting improved in 1933 when the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> (then responsible for providing equipment and personnel for the Royal Navy's <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Air_Arm" title="Fleet Air Arm">Fleet Air Arm</a>) established a station at the Royal Naval Dockyard to repair <a href="/wiki/Floatplane" title="Floatplane">float planes</a> (and supply replacements) for the fleet. In 1936, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Luft_Hansa" title="Deutsche Luft Hansa">Luft Hansa</a> began to experiment with seaplane flights from <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> with continuation flights to New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1937, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Airways" title="Imperial Airways">Imperial Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American Airways</a> began operating scheduled <a href="/wiki/Flying_boat" title="Flying boat">flying boat</a> airline services from New York and <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a> to <a href="/wiki/Darrell%27s_Island,_Bermuda" title="Darrell&#39;s Island, Bermuda">Darrell's Island, Bermuda</a>. In 1948, a regularly scheduled commercial airline service began to operate, using land-based aeroplanes landing at <a href="/wiki/Kindley_Air_Force_Base" title="Kindley Air Force Base">Kindley Field</a> (now <a href="/wiki/L.F._Wade_International_Airport" title="L.F. Wade International Airport">L.F. Wade International Airport</a>), helping tourism to reach its peak in the 1960s–1970s. By the end of the 1970s, however, international business had supplanted tourism as the dominant sector of Bermuda's economy.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Winston_Churchill_visiting_Bermuda_for_the_Wetern_Summit_in_December_1953.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Winston_Churchill_visiting_Bermuda_for_the_Wetern_Summit_in_December_1953.jpg/220px-Winston_Churchill_visiting_Bermuda_for_the_Wetern_Summit_in_December_1953.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Winston_Churchill_visiting_Bermuda_for_the_Wetern_Summit_in_December_1953.jpg/330px-Winston_Churchill_visiting_Bermuda_for_the_Wetern_Summit_in_December_1953.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Winston_Churchill_visiting_Bermuda_for_the_Wetern_Summit_in_December_1953.jpg/440px-Winston_Churchill_visiting_Bermuda_for_the_Wetern_Summit_in_December_1953.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3846" data-file-height="2565" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Winston_Churchill_visiting_Bermuda_for_the_Wetern_Summit_in_December_1953.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winston Churchill in Bermuda in December 1953 for the Bermuda Summit</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Queen_of_Bermuda_in_Bermuda,_late_1952_or_very_early_1953.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/The_Queen_of_Bermuda_in_Bermuda%2C_late_1952_or_very_early_1953.jpg/220px-The_Queen_of_Bermuda_in_Bermuda%2C_late_1952_or_very_early_1953.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/The_Queen_of_Bermuda_in_Bermuda%2C_late_1952_or_very_early_1953.jpg/330px-The_Queen_of_Bermuda_in_Bermuda%2C_late_1952_or_very_early_1953.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/The_Queen_of_Bermuda_in_Bermuda%2C_late_1952_or_very_early_1953.jpg/440px-The_Queen_of_Bermuda_in_Bermuda%2C_late_1952_or_very_early_1953.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3761" data-file-height="2535" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Queen_of_Bermuda_in_Bermuda,_late_1952_or_very_early_1953.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/SS_Queen_of_Bermuda" title="SS Queen of Bermuda">SS&#160;<i>Queen of Bermuda</i></a> in Hamilton Harbour, c. Dec 1952 / Jan 1953</div></div></div>
<p>The Royal Naval Dockyard, and the attendant military garrison, continued to be important to Bermuda's economy until the mid-20th century. In addition to considerable building work, the armed forces needed to source food and other materials from local vendors. Beginning in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, US military installations were also located in Bermuda, including a <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Bermuda_Annex" title="Naval Air Station Bermuda Annex">naval air station</a> and <a href="/wiki/USN_Submarine_Base,_Ordnance_Island,_Bermuda" title="USN Submarine Base, Ordnance Island, Bermuda">submarine base</a> along with US Army air, anti-aircraft, and coast artillery forces. The Army forces were under the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Base_Command" title="Bermuda Base Command">Bermuda Base Command</a> during the war, with some shifting and renaming of bases between the US Army, Navy, and Air Force postwar. The American military presence lasted until 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-bermuda-online.org_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bermuda-online.org-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Universal adult suffrage and the development of a two-party political system took place in the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda_9-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Universal suffrage was adopted as part of Bermuda's Constitution in 1967; voting had previously been dependent on a certain level of property ownership.
</p><p>On 10 March 1973, the governor of Bermuda, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Sharples" title="Richard Sharples">Richard Sharples</a>, was assassinated by local <a href="/wiki/Black_Power_movement" title="Black Power movement">Black Power</a> militants during a period of civil unrest.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda_9-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Some moves were made towards possible independence for the islands, however this was decisively rejected in a referendum in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda_9-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_Britannica_-_Bermuda-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Bermuda" title="Geography of Bermuda">Geography of Bermuda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_top_of_Gibbs_Lighthouse_Bermuda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/View_from_top_of_Gibbs_Lighthouse_Bermuda.jpg/180px-View_from_top_of_Gibbs_Lighthouse_Bermuda.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/View_from_top_of_Gibbs_Lighthouse_Bermuda.jpg/270px-View_from_top_of_Gibbs_Lighthouse_Bermuda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/View_from_top_of_Gibbs_Lighthouse_Bermuda.jpg/360px-View_from_top_of_Gibbs_Lighthouse_Bermuda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_top_of_Gibbs_Lighthouse_Bermuda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View from the top of Gibb's Hill Lighthouse</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_oli_2014275_lrg-cropped.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Bermuda_oli_2014275_lrg-cropped.png/180px-Bermuda_oli_2014275_lrg-cropped.png" decoding="async" width="180" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Bermuda_oli_2014275_lrg-cropped.png/270px-Bermuda_oli_2014275_lrg-cropped.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Bermuda_oli_2014275_lrg-cropped.png/360px-Bermuda_oli_2014275_lrg-cropped.png 2x" data-file-width="3448" data-file-height="2760" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_oli_2014275_lrg-cropped.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Landsat 8 satellite image</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_topographic_map-en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Bermuda_topographic_map-en.png/180px-Bermuda_topographic_map-en.png" decoding="async" width="180" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Bermuda_topographic_map-en.png/270px-Bermuda_topographic_map-en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Bermuda_topographic_map-en.png/360px-Bermuda_topographic_map-en.png 2x" data-file-width="2580" data-file-height="1820" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_topographic_map-en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographic map of Bermuda</div></div></div>
<p>Bermuda is a group of low-forming volcanoes in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, near the western edge of the <a href="/wiki/Sargasso_Sea" title="Sargasso Sea">Sargasso Sea</a>, roughly 578 nautical miles (1,070&#160;km; 665&#160;mi) east-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras" title="Cape Hatteras">Cape Hatteras</a><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> on the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Banks" title="Outer Banks">Outer Banks</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> which is the nearest landmass.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although usually referred to in the singular, the territory consists of <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Bermuda" title="List of islands of Bermuda">181 islands</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Rybeck_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rybeck-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> with a total area of 53.3 square kilometres (20.6 square miles).<sup id="cite_ref-Rybeck_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rybeck-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The largest island is Main Island, sometimes called Bermuda. Eight of the larger, populated islands are connected by bridges.<sup id="cite_ref-Rybeck_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rybeck-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The territory is largely low-lying, with the tallest peak being <a href="/wiki/Town_Hill,_Bermuda" title="Town Hill, Bermuda">Town Hill</a> on Main Island at 79m.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-highest_point_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highest_point-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The territory's coastline is 103&#160;km (64&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite the small land mass, some place names are repeated: two islands named Long Island, three bays named Long Bay (on Somerset, Main, and Cooper's islands), two Horseshoe Bays (one in Southampton, on the Main Island, the other at Morgan's Point, formerly Tucker's Island), two roads through cuttings called Khyber Pass, one in Warwick, the other in St. George's Parish, and two <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Bermuda" title="St. George&#39;s, Bermuda">St George's Towns</a> on <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Island,_Bermuda" title="St. George&#39;s Island, Bermuda">St George's Island</a> in <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Parish,_Bermuda" title="St. George&#39;s Parish, Bermuda">St George's Parish</a>, each known as St George's. There is a <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Parish,_Bermuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamilton Parish, Bermuda">Hamilton Parish</a> in addition to the City of Hamilton in <a href="/wiki/Pembroke_Parish,_Bermuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Pembroke Parish, Bermuda">Pembroke Parish</a>.
</p><p>Bermuda gives its name to the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Triangle" title="Bermuda Triangle">Bermuda Triangle</a>, a region of sea in which, according to legend, a number of aircraft and surface vessels have disappeared under supposedly unexplained or mysterious circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-navy,1996_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-navy,1996-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> However the concept is criticised by several academics as being spurious and exaggerated.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kusche,_1975_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kusche,_1975-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bermuda's pink sand beaches and clear, <a href="/wiki/Cerulean" title="Cerulean">cerulean</a> blue ocean waters are popular with tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Many of Bermuda's hotels are located along the south shore of the island. In addition to its beaches, there are a number of sightseeing attractions. Historic St George's is a designated <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>. <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">Scuba</a> divers can explore numerous <a href="/wiki/Shipwreck" title="Shipwreck">wrecks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coral_reefs" class="mw-redirect" title="Coral reefs">coral reefs</a> in relatively shallow water (typically 30–40&#160;ft or 9–12&#160;m in depth), with virtually unlimited visibility. Many nearby reefs are readily accessible from shore by <a href="/wiki/Snorkelling" class="mw-redirect" title="Snorkelling">snorkellers</a>, especially at <a href="/wiki/Church_Bay,_Bermuda" title="Church Bay, Bermuda">Church Bay</a>.
</p><p>Bermuda's most popular visitor attraction is the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Dockyard,_Bermuda" title="Royal Naval Dockyard, Bermuda">Royal Naval Dockyard</a>, which includes the Bermuda Maritime Museum.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Other attractions include the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Aquarium,_Museum_and_Zoo" title="Bermuda Aquarium, Museum and Zoo">Bermuda Aquarium, Museum and Zoo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Bermuda Underwater Exploration Institute, the Botanical Gardens and <a href="/wiki/Masterworks_Museum_of_Bermuda_Art" title="Masterworks Museum of Bermuda Art">Masterworks Museum of Bermuda Art</a>, lighthouses, and the Crystal Caves with <a href="/wiki/Stalactites" class="mw-redirect" title="Stalactites">stalactites</a> and underground saltwater pools.
</p><p>It is not possible to rent a car on the island; public transport and taxis are available or visitors can hire <a href="/wiki/Scooter_(motorcycle)" title="Scooter (motorcycle)">scooters</a> for use as private transport.<sup id="cite_ref-Rybeck_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rybeck-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NOAA_Ocean_Explorer_Bermuda_Geologic_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/NOAA_Ocean_Explorer_Bermuda_Geologic_Map.png/220px-NOAA_Ocean_Explorer_Bermuda_Geologic_Map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/NOAA_Ocean_Explorer_Bermuda_Geologic_Map.png/330px-NOAA_Ocean_Explorer_Bermuda_Geologic_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/NOAA_Ocean_Explorer_Bermuda_Geologic_Map.png/440px-NOAA_Ocean_Explorer_Bermuda_Geologic_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="654" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NOAA_Ocean_Explorer_Bermuda_Geologic_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NOAA Ocean Explorer Bermuda Geologic Map. where red denotes the Walsingham Formation, purple denotes the Town Hill and Belmont Formations, green denotes the Rocky Bay and Southampton Formations, and white is fill associated with the airport</div></div></div>
<p>Bermuda consists of more than 150 <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> islands, but 5 main islands, along the southern margin of the Bermuda Platform, which is one of three topographic highs found on the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Pedestal" title="Bermuda Pedestal">Bermuda Pedestal</a>. This Bermuda Pedestal sits atop the Bermuda Rise, a mid-basin swell surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Abyssal_plain" title="Abyssal plain">abyssal plains</a>. Initial uplift of this rise occurred in the Middle to <a href="/wiki/Late_Eocene" class="mw-redirect" title="Late Eocene">Late Eocene</a> and concluded by the <a href="/wiki/Late_Oligocene" class="mw-redirect" title="Late Oligocene">Late Oligocene</a>, when it subsided below sea level. The volcanic rocks associated with this rise are <a href="/wiki/Tholeiitic_magma_series" title="Tholeiitic magma series">tholeiitic lavas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intrusive_rock" title="Intrusive rock">intrusive</a> <a href="/wiki/Lamprophyre" title="Lamprophyre">lamprophyre</a> sheets, which form a volcanic basement, on average, 50 m below the island <a href="/wiki/Carbonate" title="Carbonate">carbonate</a> surface.<sup id="cite_ref-Vacher_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vacher-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The limestones of Bermuda consist of <a href="/wiki/Calcarenite" title="Calcarenite">biocalcarenites</a> with minor <a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(geology)" title="Conglomerate (geology)">conglomerates</a>. The portion of Bermuda above sea level consists of rocks deposited by <a href="/wiki/Aeolian_processes" title="Aeolian processes">Aeolian processes</a>. These <a href="/wiki/Eolianite" title="Eolianite">eolianites</a> are actually the <a href="/wiki/Type_locality_(geology)" title="Type locality (geology)">type locality</a>, and formed during <a href="/wiki/Interglaciation" class="mw-redirect" title="Interglaciation">interglaciations</a>, and are laced by red <a href="/wiki/Paleosol" title="Paleosol">paleosols</a>, also referred to as geosols or terra rossas, indicative of <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Saharan</a> <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_dust" class="mw-redirect" title="Atmospheric dust">atmospheric dust</a> and forming during <a href="/wiki/Glacial_stage" class="mw-redirect" title="Glacial stage">glacial stages</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Stratigraphic_column" title="Stratigraphic column">stratigraphic column</a> starts with the Walsingham <a href="/wiki/Formation_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Formation (geology)">Formation</a>, overlain by the Castle Harbour Geosol, the Lower and Upper Town Hill Formations separated by the Harbour Road Geosol, the Ord Road Geosol, the Belmont Formation, the Shore Hills Geosol, the Rocky Bay Formation, and the Southampton Formation.<sup id="cite_ref-Vacher_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vacher-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The older eolianite ridges (Older Bermuda) are more rounded and subdued compared to the outer coastline (Younger Bermuda). Thus, post deposition morphology includes chemical <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a>, with inshore water bodies demonstrating much of Bermuda is partially drowned <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a>. The Walsingham Formation is a clear example, constituting the cave district around Castle Harbour. The Upper Town Hill Formation forms the core of the Main Island, and prominent hills such as Town Hill, Knapton Hill, and St. David's Lighthouse, while the highest hills, Gibbs Hill Lighthouse, are due to the Southampton Formation.<sup id="cite_ref-Vacher_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vacher-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bermuda has two major <a href="/wiki/Aquifer" title="Aquifer">aquifers</a>, the Langton Aquifer located within the Southampton, Rocky Bay and Belmont Formations, and the Brighton Aquifer located within the Town Hill Formation. Four freshwater <a href="/wiki/Lens_(hydrology)" title="Lens (hydrology)">lenses</a> occur in Bermuda, with the Central Lens being the largest on Main Island, containing an area of 7.2&#160;km<sup>2</sup> and a thickness greater than 10 m.<sup id="cite_ref-Vacher_49-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vacher-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Bermuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Bermuda">Climate of Bermuda</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bermuda_hurricanes" title="List of Bermuda hurricanes">List of Bermuda hurricanes</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_wv.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Bermuda_wv.jpg/220px-Bermuda_wv.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Bermuda_wv.jpg/330px-Bermuda_wv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Bermuda_wv.jpg/440px-Bermuda_wv.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_wv.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Residential scene in Bermuda</div></div></div>
<p>Bermuda has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <b>Cfa</b>), bordering very closely on a  <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <b>Af</b>). Bermuda is warmed by the nearby <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>, and low latitude. The islands may experience modestly cooler temperatures in January, February, and March (average 63&#160;°F (17&#160;°C)).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> There has never been snow, a frost or freeze on record in Bermuda.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Summertime <a href="/wiki/Heat_index" title="Heat index">heat index</a> in Bermuda can be high, although mid-August temperatures rarely exceed 30&#160;°C (86&#160;°F). The highest recorded temperature was 34&#160;°C (93&#160;°F) in August 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The average annual temperature of the Atlantic Ocean around Bermuda is 22.8&#160;°C (73.0&#160;°F), from 18.6&#160;°C (65.5&#160;°F) in February to 28.2&#160;°C (82.8&#160;°F) in August.<sup id="cite_ref-BWS_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BWS-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bermuda is in the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">hurricane belt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Along the Gulf Stream, it is often directly in the path of hurricanes recurving in the westerlies, although they usually begin to weaken as they approach Bermuda, whose small size means that direct <a href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfalls</a> of hurricanes are rare. The most recent hurricanes to cause significant damage to Bermuda were <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir–Simpson Hurricane Scale">category 2</a> <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gonzalo" title="Hurricane Gonzalo">Hurricane Gonzalo</a> on 18 October 2014 and <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir–Simpson Hurricane Scale">category 3</a> <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Nicole" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Nicole">Hurricane Nicole</a> on 14 October 2016, both of which struck the island directly. Before that, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fabian" title="Hurricane Fabian">Hurricane Fabian</a> on 5 September 2003 was the last major hurricane to hit Bermuda directly.
</p><p>With no rivers or freshwater lakes, the only source of fresh water is rainfall, which is collected on roofs and catchments (or drawn from underground lenses) and stored in tanks.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Each dwelling usually has at least one of these tanks forming part of its foundation. The law requires that each household collect rainwater that is piped down from the roof of each house. Average monthly rainfall is highest in October, at over 6 inches (150&#160;mm), and lowest in April and May.
</p>
