<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Bermuda" title="Wildlife of Bermuda">Wildlife of Bermuda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Juvenile_Bermuda_Cedar_at_Ferry_Reach.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Juvenile_Bermuda_Cedar_at_Ferry_Reach.jpg/220px-Juvenile_Bermuda_Cedar_at_Ferry_Reach.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Juvenile_Bermuda_Cedar_at_Ferry_Reach.jpg/330px-Juvenile_Bermuda_Cedar_at_Ferry_Reach.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Juvenile_Bermuda_Cedar_at_Ferry_Reach.jpg/440px-Juvenile_Bermuda_Cedar_at_Ferry_Reach.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Juvenile_Bermuda_Cedar_at_Ferry_Reach.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Young Bermuda cedar tree at <a href="/wiki/Ferry_Reach,_Bermuda" title="Ferry Reach, Bermuda">Ferry Reach</a></div></div></div>
<p>When discovered, Bermuda was uninhabited by humans and mostly dominated by forests of <a href="/wiki/Juniperus_bermudiana" title="Juniperus bermudiana">Bermuda cedar</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangrove</a> <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">marshes</a> along its shores.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Only 165 of the island's current 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Vascular_plant" title="Vascular plant">vascular plant</a> species are considered <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_(ecology)" title="Indigenous (ecology)">native</a>; fifteen of those, including the eponymous cedar, are <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The semi-tropical climate of Bermuda allowed settlers to introduce many species of trees and plants to the island. Today, many types of palm trees, fruit trees, and bananas grow on Bermuda.
</p><p>The only <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_(ecology)" title="Indigenous (ecology)">indigenous</a> <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a> of Bermuda are five species of <a href="/wiki/Bat" title="Bat">bat</a>, all of which are also found in the eastern United States: <i><a href="/wiki/Lasionycteris_noctivagans" class="mw-redirect" title="Lasionycteris noctivagans">Lasionycteris noctivagans</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lasiurus_borealis" class="mw-redirect" title="Lasiurus borealis">Lasiurus borealis</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lasiurus_cinereus" class="mw-redirect" title="Lasiurus cinereus">Lasiurus cinereus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lasiurus_seminolus" class="mw-redirect" title="Lasiurus seminolus">Lasiurus seminolus</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Perimyotis_subflavus" class="mw-redirect" title="Perimyotis subflavus">Perimyotis subflavus</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Other commonly known fauna of Bermuda include its national bird, the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_petrel" title="Bermuda petrel">Bermuda petrel</a> or cahow, which was rediscovered in 1951 after having been thought extinct since the 1620s.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The cahow is important as an example of a <a href="/wiki/Lazarus_taxon" title="Lazarus taxon">Lazarus</a> species, hence the government has a programme to protect it, including the restoration its habitat areas.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_rock_skink" title="Bermuda rock skink">Bermuda skink</a> (or <i>rock lizard</i>) was long thought to have been the only indigenous land vertebrate of Bermuda, discounting the marine turtles that lay their eggs on its beaches. However, scientists have recently discovered through genetic DNA studies that a species of <a href="/wiki/Turtle" title="Turtle">turtle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Diamondback_terrapin" title="Diamondback terrapin">diamondback terrapin</a>, previously thought to have been introduced to the archipelago, actually pre-dated the arrival of humans.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> As this species spends most of its time in brackish ponds, some argue that it should be classified as a land vertebrate to compete with the skink's unique status.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Bermuda" title="Demographics of Bermuda">Demographics of Bermuda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibb%27s_Hill_Lighthouse,_Bermuda_July_2015_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Gibb%27s_Hill_Lighthouse%2C_Bermuda_July_2015_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Gibb%27s_Hill_Lighthouse%2C_Bermuda_July_2015_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Gibb%27s_Hill_Lighthouse%2C_Bermuda_July_2015_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Gibb%27s_Hill_Lighthouse%2C_Bermuda_July_2015_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Gibb%27s_Hill_Lighthouse%2C_Bermuda_July_2015_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Gibb%27s_Hill_Lighthouse%2C_Bermuda_July_2015_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibb%27s_Hill_Lighthouse,_Bermuda_July_2015_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of Bermuda from <a href="/wiki/Gibbs_Hill_Lighthouse" title="Gibbs Hill Lighthouse">Gibbs Hill Lighthouse</a> in July 2015.</div></div></div>
<p>Bermuda's 2010 Census put Bermuda's population at 64,237 and, with an area of 53.2&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (20.5&#160;sq&#160;mi), it has a calculated population density of 1207/km². As of July 2018, the population is estimated to be 71,176.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The racial makeup of Bermuda as recorded by the 2010 census, was 54% Black, 31% White, 8% multiracial, 4% Asian, and 4% other races, although these numbers are based on self-identification, and the majority of those who answered "black" having any mixture of black, white or other ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-Bermuda_2010_Census_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bermuda_2010_Census-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Native-born Bermudians made up 67% of the population, compared to 29% non-natives.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Theresa%27s_Cathedral_chapel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/St._Theresa%27s_Cathedral_chapel.jpg/170px-St._Theresa%27s_Cathedral_chapel.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/St._Theresa%27s_Cathedral_chapel.jpg/255px-St._Theresa%27s_Cathedral_chapel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/St._Theresa%27s_Cathedral_chapel.jpg/340px-St._Theresa%27s_Cathedral_chapel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="3648" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St._Theresa%27s_Cathedral_chapel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The image of the <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_Senhor_Santo_Cristo_dos_Milagres" title="Cult of Senhor Santo Cristo dos Milagres">Lord Holy Christ of the Miracles</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Bermuda" title="Hamilton, Bermuda">Hamilton</a>, venerated by <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azoreans</a> in Bermuda.</div></div></div>
<p>The island experienced large-scale immigration over the 20th century, especially after the Second World War. Bermuda has a diverse population including both those with relatively deep roots in Bermuda extending back for centuries, and newer communities whose ancestry results from recent immigration, especially from Britain, North America, the West Indies, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Portugal" title="List of islands of Portugal">Portuguese Atlantic islands</a> (especially the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>), although these groups are steadily merging. About 64% of the population identified themselves with Bermudian ancestry in 2010, which was an increase from the 51% who did so in the 2000 census. Those identifying with British ancestry dropped by 1% to 11% (although those born in Britain remain the largest non-native group at 3,942 persons). The number of people born in Canada declined by 13%. Those who reported West Indian ancestry were 13%. The number of people born in the West Indies actually increased by 538. A significant segment of the population is of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> ancestry (25%), the result of immigration over the past 160 years,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> of whom 79% have residency status. In June 2018, Premier <a href="/wiki/Edward_David_Burt" title="Edward David Burt">Edward David Burt</a> announced that 4 November 2019 "will be declared a public holiday to mark the 170th anniversary of the arrival of the first Portuguese immigrants in Bermuda" due to the significant impact that Portuguese immigration has had on the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Those first immigrants arrived from <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> aboard the vessel the Golden Rule on 4 November 1849.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are also several thousand <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriate</a> workers, principally from Britain, Canada, the West Indies, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and the United States, reside in Bermuda. They are primarily engaged in specialised professions such as accounting, finance, and insurance. Others are employed in various trades, such as hotels, restaurants, construction, and landscaping services. Of the total workforce of 38,947 persons in 2005, government employment figures stated that 11,223 (29%) were non-Bermudians.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The predominant language on Bermuda is <a href="/wiki/Bermudian_English" title="Bermudian English">Bermudian English</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> It exhibits characteristics of British, West Indian, and American English. <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a> spellings and conventions are used in print media and formal written communications.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> is also spoken by migrants from the Azores and Madeira and their descendants.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">
<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:Red"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 101.26459941541px; border-left-color:Grey"></div>

<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Grey"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:94.709830499474px 32.094360980721px 0 0; border-top-color:Blue"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Blue"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:62.278778048811px 78.239081057659px 0 0; border-top-color:Yellow"></div>

</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religion in Bermuda (2010)<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Purple; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> (46.2%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> (14.5%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other Christian (9.1%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Grey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Unaffiliated (17.8%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other religion (12.4%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is by far the largest religion on Bermuda.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Various Protestant denominations are dominant at 46.2% (including Anglican 15.8%, African Methodist Episcopal 8.6%, Seventh Day Adventist 6.7%, Pentecostal 3.5%, Methodist 2.7%, Presbyterian 2.0%, Church of God 1.6%, Baptist 1.2%, Salvation Army 1.1%, Brethren 1.0%, other Protestant 2.0%).<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Roman Catholics form 14.5%, Jehovah's Witnesses 1.3%, and other Christians 9.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The rest of the population are Muslim 1%, other 3.9%, none 17.8%, or unspecified 6.2% (2010 est.).<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bermuda" title="Politics of Bermuda">Politics of Bermuda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/220px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/330px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" data-file-width="2206" data-file-height="1358" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the European Union in the world with <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">overseas countries and territories and outermost regions</a></div></div></div>
<p>Bermuda is an <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British Overseas Territory">Overseas Territory</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Executive authority in Bermuda is vested in the British monarch (currently <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>) and is exercised on her behalf by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Bermuda" title="Governor of Bermuda">governor of Bermuda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The governor is appointed by the queen on the advice of the <a href="/wiki/British_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="British Government">British Government</a>. Since December 2016, the governor has been <a href="/wiki/John_Rankin_(diplomat)" title="John Rankin (diplomat)">John Rankin</a>; he was sworn in on 5 December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> There is also a deputy governor (currently David Arkley <a href="/wiki/Justice_of_the_Peace" class="mw-redirect" title="Justice of the Peace">JP</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Defence and foreign affairs are the responsibility of the United Kingdom, which also retains responsibility to ensure good government and must approve any changes to the Constitution of Bermuda. Bermuda is Britain's oldest overseas territory. In 1620, a Royal Proclamation granted Bermuda limited self-governance; its <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Bermuda" title="Parliament of Bermuda">Parliament</a> is the fifth oldest in the world, behind the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tynwald" title="Tynwald">Tynwald</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Althing" title="Althing">Althing</a> of <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sejm" title="Sejm">Sejm</a> of Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda-The_State_House.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Bermuda-The_State_House.jpg/220px-Bermuda-The_State_House.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Bermuda-The_State_House.jpg/330px-Bermuda-The_State_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Bermuda-The_State_House.jpg/440px-Bermuda-The_State_House.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="337" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda-The_State_House.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/State_House,_Bermuda" title="State House, Bermuda">State House</a> in <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Bermuda" title="St. George&#39;s, Bermuda">St. George's</a>, the home of Bermuda's <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Bermuda" title="Parliament of Bermuda">parliament</a> between 1620 and 1815.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sessions_House,_Hamilton,_Bermuda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Sessions_House%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg/220px-Sessions_House%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Sessions_House%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg/330px-Sessions_House%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Sessions_House%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg/440px-Sessions_House%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sessions_House,_Hamilton,_Bermuda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Bermuda" title="House of Assembly of Bermuda">Sessions House</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Bermuda" title="Hamilton, Bermuda">Hamilton</a>, current home of the House of Assembly and the Supreme Court.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Constitution_of_Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Constitution of Bermuda (page does not exist)">Constitution of Bermuda</a> came into force in 1968 and has been amended several times since then.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The head of government is the <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Bermuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Premier of Bermuda">Premier of Bermuda</a>; a cabinet is nominated by the premier and appointed officially by the governor.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The legislative branch consists of a <a href="/wiki/Bicameral_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral parliament">bicameral parliament</a> modelled on the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Bermuda" title="Senate of Bermuda">Senate</a> is the upper house, consisting of 11 members appointed by the governor on the advice of the premier and the leader of the opposition. The <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Bermuda" title="House of Assembly of Bermuda">House of Assembly</a>, or lower house, has 36 members, elected by the eligible voting populace in secret ballot to represent geographically defined constituencies.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Bermuda" title="Elections in Bermuda">Elections</a> must be called at no more than five-year intervals. The <a href="/wiki/Bermudian_general_election,_2017" class="mw-redirect" title="Bermudian general election, 2017">most recent</a> took place on 18 July 2017. Following this election, the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Labour_Party_(Bermuda)" title="Progressive Labour Party (Bermuda)">Progressive Labour Party</a> took power, with <a href="/wiki/David_Burt" title="David Burt">David Burt</a> succeeding <a href="/wiki/Michael_Dunkley" title="Michael Dunkley">Michael Dunkley</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/One_Bermuda_Alliance" title="One Bermuda Alliance">One Bermuda Alliance</a>, as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premiers_of_Bermuda" title="List of Premiers of Bermuda">Premier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are few accredited diplomats in Bermuda. The United States maintains the largest diplomatic mission in Bermuda, comprising both the United States Consulate and the <a href="/wiki/US_Customs_and_Border_Protection" class="mw-redirect" title="US Customs and Border Protection">US Customs and Border Protection</a> Services at the <a href="/wiki/L.F._Wade_International_Airport" title="L.F. Wade International Airport">L.F. Wade International Airport</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The United States is Bermuda's largest trading partner (providing over 71% of total imports, 85% of tourist visitors, and an estimated $163&#160;billion of US capital in the Bermuda insurance/re-insurance industry), and an estimated 5% of Bermuda residents are US citizens, representing 14% of all foreign-born persons.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Bermuda" title="Administrative divisions of Bermuda">Administrative divisions of Bermuda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda-divmap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bermuda-divmap.png/220px-Bermuda-divmap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bermuda-divmap.png/330px-Bermuda-divmap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bermuda-divmap.png/440px-Bermuda-divmap.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="597" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda-divmap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Parishes of Bermuda.</div></div></div>
<p>Bermuda is divided into nine <a href="/wiki/Parish_(administrative_division)" title="Parish (administrative division)">parishes</a> and two incorporated <a href="/wiki/Municipalities" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities">municipalities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bermuda's nine parishes are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Devonshire_Parish" title="Devonshire Parish">Devonshire</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Parish" title="Hamilton Parish">Hamilton</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paget_Parish" title="Paget Parish">Paget</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pembroke_Parish" title="Pembroke Parish">Pembroke</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sandys_Parish" title="Sandys Parish">Sandys</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Smith%27s_Parish" title="Smith&#39;s Parish">Smith's</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Southampton_Parish,_Bermuda" title="Southampton Parish, Bermuda">Southampton</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Parish,_Bermuda" title="St. George&#39;s Parish, Bermuda">St George's</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Warwick_Parish" title="Warwick Parish">Warwick</a></li></ul>
<p>Bermuda's two incorporated municipalities are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Bermuda" title="Hamilton, Bermuda">Hamilton</a> (city)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Bermuda" title="St. George&#39;s, Bermuda">St George's</a> (town)</li></ul>
<p>Bermuda's two informal villages are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Flatts_Village,_Bermuda" title="Flatts Village, Bermuda">Flatts Village</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Somerset_Village,_Bermuda" title="Somerset Village, Bermuda">Somerset Village</a></li></ul>
<p>Jones Village in Warwick, Cashew City (St. George's), Claytown (Hamilton), Middle Town (Pembroke), and <a href="/wiki/Tucker%27s_Town" class="mw-redirect" title="Tucker&#39;s Town">Tucker's Town</a> (St. George's) are neighbourhoods; Dandy Town and North Village are sports clubs, and Harbour View Village is a small <a href="/wiki/Public_housing" title="Public housing">public housing</a> development.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a British Overseas Territory, Bermuda does not have a seat in the <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_United_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="General Assembly of the United Nations">United Nations</a>; it is represented by Britain in matters of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">foreign affairs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> To promote its economic interests abroad, Bermuda maintains representative offices in cities such as London<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bermuda's proximity to the US had made it attractive as the site for summit conferences between British Prime Ministers and US Presidents. The first summit was held in December 1953, at the insistence of Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, to discuss relations with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. Participants included Churchill, US President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> and French Premier <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Laniel" title="Joseph Laniel">Joseph Laniel</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 1957 a second summit conference was held. The British Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Macmillan" title="Harold Macmillan">Harold Macmillan</a>, arrived earlier than President Eisenhower, to demonstrate they were meeting on British territory, as tensions were still high regarding the previous year's conflict over the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>. Macmillan returned in 1961 for the third summit with President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>. The meeting was called to discuss Cold War tensions arising from construction of the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Visitors_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visitors-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most recent summit conference in Bermuda between the two powers occurred in 1990, when British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> met US President <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Visitors_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Visitors-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Direct meetings between the president of the United States and the <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Bermuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Premier of Bermuda">premier of Bermuda</a> have been rare. The most recent meeting was on 23 June 2008, between Premier <a href="/wiki/Ewart_Brown" title="Ewart Brown">Ewart Brown</a> and President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>. Prior to this, the leaders of Bermuda and the United States had not met at the White House since a 1996 meeting between Premier David Saul and President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rg_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bermuda has also joined several other nations in efforts to protect the <a href="/wiki/Sargasso_Sea" title="Sargasso Sea">Sargasso Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013 and 2017 Bermuda chaired the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Overseas_Territories_Association" title="United Kingdom Overseas Territories Association">United Kingdom Overseas Territories Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Asylum_offer_to_four_former_Guant.C3.A1namo_detainees"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Asylum_offer_to_four_former_Guantánamo_detainees">Asylum offer to four former Guantánamo detainees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Asylum offer to four former Guantánamo detainees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_detainees_at_Guantanamo_Bay#Bermuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Uyghur detainees at Guantanamo Bay">Uyghur detainees at Guantanamo Bay: Bermuda</a></div>
<p>On 11 June 2009, four <a href="/wiki/Uyghur_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Uyghur people">Uyghurs</a> who had been held in the United States <a href="/wiki/Guant%C3%A1namo_Bay_detention_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Guantánamo Bay detention camp">Guantánamo Bay detention camp</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, were transferred to Bermuda.<sup id="cite_ref-AssociatedPress2009-06-11_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AssociatedPress2009-06-11-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RadioFreeAsia2009-06-11_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RadioFreeAsia2009-06-11-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RoyalGazette2009-06-11a_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RoyalGazette2009-06-11a-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RoyalGazette2009-06-11b_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RoyalGazette2009-06-11b-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The four men were among 22 Uyghurs who claimed to be refugees who were captured in 2001 in Pakistan after fleeing the <a href="/wiki/American_aerial_bombardment_of_Afghanistan" class="mw-redirect" title="American aerial bombardment of Afghanistan">American aerial bombardment of Afghanistan</a>. They were accused of training to assist the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a>'s military. They were cleared as safe for release from Guantánamo in 2005 or 2006, but US domestic law prohibited deporting them back to China, their country of citizenship, because the US government determined that China was <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_China" title="Human rights in China">likely to violate</a> their human rights.
</p><p>In September 2008, the men were cleared of all suspicion and Judge Ricardo Urbina in Washington ordered their release. Congressional opposition to their admittance to the United States was very strong<sup id="cite_ref-AssociatedPress2009-06-11_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AssociatedPress2009-06-11-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and the US failed to find a home for them until Bermuda and <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a> agreed to accept the 22 men in June 2009.
</p><p>The secret bilateral discussions that led to prisoner transfers between the US and the devolved Bermuda government sparked diplomatic ire from the United Kingdom, which was not consulted on the move despite Bermuda being a British territory. The British Foreign Office issued the following statement:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886047036"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We've underlined to the Bermuda Government that they should have consulted with the United Kingdom as to whether this falls within their competence or is a security issue, for which the Bermuda Government do not have delegated responsibility. We have made clear to the Bermuda Government the need for a security assessment, which we are now helping them to carry out, and we will decide on further steps as appropriate.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>In August 2018, the four Uyghurs were granted limited citizenship in Bermuda. The men now have the same rights as Bermudians except the right to vote.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Caribbean_Community">Caribbean Community</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Caribbean Community">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_passport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Bermuda_passport.jpg/150px-Bermuda_passport.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Bermuda_passport.jpg/225px-Bermuda_passport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Bermuda_passport.jpg/300px-Bermuda_passport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="686" data-file-height="988" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bermuda_passport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Bermudian_passport" class="mw-redirect" title="Bermudian passport">Bermudian passport</a></div></div></div>
<p>Bermuda became an associate member of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM) in July 2003, despite not being in the Caribbean region.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>CARICOM is a <a href="/wiki/Socio-economic" class="mw-redirect" title="Socio-economic">socio-economic</a> bloc of nations in or near the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. Other outlying member states include the Co-operative Republic of <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> in South America, and <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> in Central America. The <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>, an associate member of CARICOM, and the Commonwealth of <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a>, a full member of CARICOM, are in the Atlantic, but close to the Caribbean. Other nearby nations or territories, such as the United States, are not members (although the US Commonwealth of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> has <a href="/wiki/Observer_status" title="Observer status">observer status</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a> announced in 2007 that they would seek ties with CARICOM). Bermuda has minimal trade with the Caribbean region, and little in common with it economically, being roughly a thousand miles from the Caribbean Sea; it joined CARICOM primarily to strengthen cultural links with the region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Among some scholars,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (August 2010)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> "the Caribbean" can be a socio-historical category, commonly referring to a cultural zone characterised by the legacy of slavery (a characteristic Bermuda shared with the Caribbean and the US) and the plantation system (which did not exist in Bermuda). It embraces the islands and parts of the neighbouring continent, and may be extended to include the Caribbean Diaspora overseas.<sup id="cite_ref-acs-aec.org_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acs-aec.org-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The PLP, which was the party in government when the decision was made to join CARICOM, has been dominated for decades by West Indians and their descendants. The prominent roles of West Indians among Bermuda's black politicians and labour activists predated party politics in Bermuda, as exemplified by Dr. <a href="/wiki/E._F._Gordon" class="mw-redirect" title="E. F. Gordon">E. F. Gordon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The late PLP leader, Dame <a href="/wiki/Lois_Browne-Evans" title="Lois Browne-Evans">Lois Browne-Evans</a>, and her <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidadian</a>-born husband, John Evans (who co-founded the <i>West Indian Association of Bermuda</i> in 1976),<sup id="cite_ref-royalgazette.com_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-royalgazette.com-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> were prominent members of this group. They have emphasised Bermuda's cultural connections with the West Indies. Many Bermudians, both black and white, who lack family connections to the West Indies have objected to this emphasis.<sup id="cite_ref-royalgazette.com_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-royalgazette.com-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The decision to join CARICOM stirred up a huge amount of debate and speculation among the Bermudian community and politicians.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Opinion polls conducted by two Bermudian newspapers, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Royal_Gazette_(Bermuda)" title="The Royal Gazette (Bermuda)">The Royal Gazette</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bermuda_Sun" class="mw-redirect" title="The Bermuda Sun">The Bermuda Sun</a></i>, showed that clear majorities of Bermudians were opposed to joining CARICOM.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The UBP, which had been in government from 1968 to 1998, argued that joining CARICOM was detrimental to Bermuda's interests:<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Bermuda's trade with the West Indies is negligible, its primary economic partners being the US, Canada, and UK (it has no direct air or shipping links to Caribbean islands);</li>
<li>CARICOM is moving towards a single economy;</li>
<li>the Caribbean islands are generally competitors to Bermuda's already ailing tourism industry; and</li>
<li>participation in CARICOM would involve considerable investment of money and the time of government officials that could more profitably be spent elsewhere.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Bermuda" title="Military of Bermuda">Military of Bermuda</a></div>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Bermuda%22">"Bermuda"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Bermuda%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Bermuda%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Bermuda%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Bermuda%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Bermuda%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
 <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BVRC-Great-War-Contingent_1914.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b2/BVRC-Great-War-Contingent_1914.jpg/220px-BVRC-Great-War-Contingent_1914.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="95" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b2/BVRC-Great-War-Contingent_1914.jpg/330px-BVRC-Great-War-Contingent_1914.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b2/BVRC-Great-War-Contingent_1914.jpg/440px-BVRC-Great-War-Contingent_1914.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="347" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BVRC-Great-War-Contingent_1914.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The First <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Volunteer_Rifle_Corps" title="Bermuda Volunteer Rifle Corps">Bermuda Volunteer Rifle Corps</a> Contingent, raised in 1914. By the war's end, the two BVRC contingents had lost over 75% of their combined strength.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rembrance_Day_Parade_Bermuda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Rembrance_Day_Parade_Bermuda.jpg/220px-Rembrance_Day_Parade_Bermuda.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Rembrance_Day_Parade_Bermuda.jpg/330px-Rembrance_Day_Parade_Bermuda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Rembrance_Day_Parade_Bermuda.jpg/440px-Rembrance_Day_Parade_Bermuda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="494" data-file-height="341" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rembrance_Day_Parade_Bermuda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Remembrance Day Parade, Hamilton, Bermuda.</div></div></div>
<p>Once known as "the Gibraltar of the West" and "Fortress Bermuda", Bermuda today is defended by British forces. For the first two centuries of settlement, the most potent armed force operating from Bermuda was its merchant shipping fleet, which turned to <a href="/wiki/Privateering" class="mw-redirect" title="Privateering">privateering</a> at every opportunity. The Bermuda government maintained a local militia. After the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, Bermuda was established as the Western Atlantic headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>. Once the Royal Navy established a base and dockyard defended by regular soldiers, however, the militias were disbanded following the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>. At the end of the 19th century, the colony raised <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Volunteer/Territorial_Army_Units_1895-1965" class="mw-redirect" title="Bermuda Volunteer/Territorial Army Units 1895-1965">volunteer units</a> to form a reserve for the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Garrison" title="Bermuda Garrison">military garrison</a>.
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Battle of the Atlantic</a></div>
<p>Due to its isolated location in the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Ocean" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic Ocean</a>, Bermuda was vital to the Allies' war effort during both <a href="/wiki/World_war" title="World war">world wars</a> of the 20th century, serving as a marshalling point for trans-Atlantic convoys, as well as a naval air base. By the Second World War, both the Royal Navy's <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Air_Arm" title="Fleet Air Arm">Fleet Air Arm</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> were operating <a href="/wiki/Seaplane" title="Seaplane">Seaplane</a> bases on Bermuda.
</p><p>In May 1940, the US requested base rights in Bermuda from the United Kingdom, but British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> was initially unwilling to accede to the American request without getting something in return.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In September 1940, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Destroyers_for_Bases_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Destroyers for Bases Agreement">Destroyers for Bases Agreement</a>, the UK granted the US base rights in Bermuda. Bermuda and <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a> were not originally included in the agreement, but both were added to it, with no war material received by the UK in exchange. One of the terms of the agreement was that the airfield the US Army built would be used jointly by the US and the UK (which it was for the duration of the war, with RAF Transport Command relocating there from <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force,_Bermuda,_1939-1945" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Air Force, Bermuda, 1939-1945">Darrell's Island</a> in 1943). The US Army established the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Base_Command" title="Bermuda Base Command">Bermuda Base Command</a> in 1941 to coordinate its <a href="/wiki/USAAF" class="mw-redirect" title="USAAF">air</a>, anti-aircraft, and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Coast_Artillery_Corps" title="United States Army Coast Artillery Corps">coast artillery</a> assets during the war. The US Navy operated a <a href="/wiki/USN_Submarine_Base,_Ordnance_Island,_Bermuda" title="USN Submarine Base, Ordnance Island, Bermuda">submarine base</a> on <a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Island,_Bermuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordnance Island, Bermuda">Ordnance Island</a> from 1942 through 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-bermuda-online.org_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bermuda-online.org-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Construction began in 1941 of two airbases consisting of 5.8&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2.2&#160;sq&#160;mi) of land, largely reclaimed from the sea. For many years, Bermuda's bases were used by <a href="/wiki/US_Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="US Air Force">US Air Force</a> transport and refuelling aircraft and by <a href="/wiki/US_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="US Navy">US Navy</a> aircraft patrolling the Atlantic for enemy submarines, first <a href="/wiki/Kriegsmarine" title="Kriegsmarine">German</a> and, later, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Navy" title="Soviet Navy">Soviet</a>. The principal installation, <a href="/wiki/Kindley_Air_Force_Base" title="Kindley Air Force Base">Kindley Air Force Base</a> on the eastern coast, was transferred to the US Navy in 1970 and redesignated <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Bermuda" title="Naval Air Station Bermuda">Naval Air Station Bermuda</a>. As a naval air station, the base continued to host both transient and deployed USN and USAF aircraft, as well as transitioning or deployed Royal Air Force and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian Forces">Canadian Forces</a> aircraft.
</p><p>The original <a href="/wiki/NAS_Bermuda" class="mw-redirect" title="NAS Bermuda">NAS Bermuda</a> on the west side of the island, a <a href="/wiki/Seaplane" title="Seaplane">seaplane</a> base until the mid-1960s, was designated as the Naval Air Station Bermuda Annex. It provided optional anchorage and/or dockage facilities for transiting US Navy, <a href="/wiki/US_Coast_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="US Coast Guard">US Coast Guard</a> and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> vessels, depending on size. An additional US Navy compound known as <a href="/wiki/Naval_Facility_Bermuda" title="Naval Facility Bermuda">Naval Facility Bermuda</a> (NAVFAC Bermuda), a submarine-detecting <a href="/wiki/SOSUS" title="SOSUS">SOSUS</a> station, was located to the west of the Annex near a Canadian Forces communications facility in the Tudor Hill area; it was converted from a US Army coast artillery bunker in 1954 and operated until 1995. Although leased for 99 years, US forces withdrew in 1995, as part of the wave of base closures following the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.
</p><p>Canada, which had operated a war-time naval base, <a href="/wiki/HMCS_Somers_Isles" title="HMCS Somers Isles">HMCS <i>Somers Isles</i></a>, on the old Royal Navy base at Convict Bay, St George's, also established a radio-listening post at Daniel's Head in the West End of the islands during this time.
</p><p>In the 1950s, after the end of World War II, the Royal Naval dockyard and the military garrison were closed. A small Royal Navy supply base, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Malabar_(shore_establishment)" class="mw-redirect" title="HMS Malabar (shore establishment)">HMS <i>Malabar</i></a>, continued to operate within the dockyard area, supporting transiting Royal Navy ships and submarines until it, too, was closed in 1995, along with the American and Canadian bases.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Ambuscade_in_Bermuda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/HMS_Ambuscade_in_Bermuda.jpg/220px-HMS_Ambuscade_in_Bermuda.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/HMS_Ambuscade_in_Bermuda.jpg/330px-HMS_Ambuscade_in_Bermuda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/HMS_Ambuscade_in_Bermuda.jpg/440px-HMS_Ambuscade_in_Bermuda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="499" data-file-height="398" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMS_Ambuscade_in_Bermuda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/HMS_Ambuscade_(F172)" title="HMS Ambuscade (F172)">HMS <i>Ambuscade</i></a> at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Dockyard,_Bermuda" title="Royal Naval Dockyard, Bermuda">Royal Naval Dockyard in 1988</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Bermudians served in the British armed forces during both <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and World War II. After the latter, Major-General <a href="/wiki/Glyn_Gilbert" title="Glyn Gilbert">Glyn Charles Anglim Gilbert</a>, Bermuda's highest-ranking soldier, was instrumental in developing the Bermuda Regiment. A number of other Bermudians and their descendants had preceded him into senior ranks, including Bahamian-born Admiral <a href="/wiki/James_Gambier,_1st_Baron_Gambier" title="James Gambier, 1st Baron Gambier">Lord Gambier</a>, and Bermudian-born <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">Royal Marines</a> Brigadier Harvey. When promoted to brigadier at age 39, following his wounding at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Anzio" title="Battle of Anzio">Anzio landings</a>, Harvey became the youngest-ever Royal Marine Brigadier. The <a href="/wiki/Cenotaph" title="Cenotaph">Cenotaph</a> in front of the Cabinet Building (in Hamilton) was erected in tribute to Bermuda's Great War dead (the tribute was later extended to Bermuda's Second World War dead) and is the site of the annual <a href="/wiki/Remembrance_Day" title="Remembrance Day">Remembrance Day</a> commemoration.
</p><p>Today, the only military unit remaining in Bermuda, other than <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Sea_Cadet_Corps" title="Bermuda Sea Cadet Corps">naval</a> and army cadet corps, is the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Regiment" class="mw-redirect" title="Bermuda Regiment">Bermuda Regiment</a>, an amalgam of the voluntary units originally formed toward the end of the 19th century. Although the Regiment's predecessors were voluntary units, the modern body is formed primarily by conscription: balloted males are required to serve for three years, two months part-time, once they turn 18.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Bermuda" title="Economy of Bermuda">Economy of Bermuda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Front_Street,_Hamilton,_Bermuda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Front_Street%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg/220px-Front_Street%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Front_Street%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg/330px-Front_Street%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Front_Street%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg/440px-Front_Street%2C_Hamilton%2C_Bermuda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Front_Street,_Hamilton,_Bermuda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Front Street, Hamilton.</div></div></div>
<p>Banking and other financial services form the largest sector of the economy at circa 85% of GDP, with tourism being the second largest industry at 5%.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Smithsonian_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smithsonian-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Industrial and agriculture activities occur, however these are on a very limited scale and Bermuda is heavily reliant on imports.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Living standards are high and as of 2019 Bermuda has the 6th highest GDP per capita in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Currency">Currency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Currency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1970 the country switched its currency from the <a href="/wiki/Bermudian_pound" title="Bermudian pound">Bermudian pound</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Bermudian_dollar" title="Bermudian dollar">Bermudian dollar</a>, which is <a href="/wiki/Fixed_exchange_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fixed exchange rate">pegged</a> at par with the US dollar. US notes and coins are used interchangeably with Bermudian notes and coins within the islands for most practical purposes; however, banks levy an exchange rate fee for the purchase of US dollars with Bermudian dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Monetary_Authority" title="Bermuda Monetary Authority">Bermuda Monetary Authority</a> is the issuing authority for all banknotes and coins, and regulates financial institutions. The Royal Naval Dockyard Museum holds a permanent exhibition of Bermuda notes and coins.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bermuda is an <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centre" title="Offshore financial centre">offshore financial centre</a>, which results from its minimal standards of business regulation/laws and direct <a href="/wiki/Taxation" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxation">taxation</a> on personal or corporate income. It has one of the highest consumption taxes in the world and taxes all imports in lieu of an income tax system. Bermuda's consumption tax is equivalent to local income tax to local residents and funds government and infrastructure expenditures. The local tax system depends upon import duties, payroll taxes and <a href="/wiki/Consumption_tax" title="Consumption tax">consumption taxes</a>. Foreign private individuals cannot easily open bank accounts or subscribe to mobile phone or internet services.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Having no corporate income tax, Bermuda is a popular <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax avoidance location</a>. <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>, for example, is known to have shifted over $10 billion in revenue to its Bermuda subsidiary utilising the <a href="/wiki/Double_Irish_arrangement" title="Double Irish arrangement">Double Irish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Sandwich" title="Dutch Sandwich">Dutch Sandwich</a> tax avoidance strategies, reducing its 2011 tax liability by $2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Large numbers of leading international insurance companies operate in Bermuda.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Those internationally owned and operated businesses that are physically based in Bermuda (around four hundred) are represented by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Association_of_Bermuda_International_Companies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Association of Bermuda International Companies (page does not exist)">Association of Bermuda International Companies</a> (ABIC). In total, over 15,000 exempted or international companies are currently registered with the <a href="/wiki/Registrar_of_Companies" title="Registrar of Companies">Registrar of Companies</a> in Bermuda, most of which hold no office space or employees.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>There are four hundred securities listed on the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Stock_Exchange" title="Bermuda Stock Exchange">Bermuda Stock Exchange</a> (BSX), of which almost three hundred are offshore funds and alternative investment structures attracted by Bermuda's regulatory environment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The Exchange specialises in listing and trading of capital market instruments such as equities, debt issues, funds (including hedge fund structures) and depository receipt programmes. The BSX is a full member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Federation_of_Exchanges" title="World Federation of Exchanges">World Federation of Exchanges</a> and is located in an <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> member nation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It also has Approved Stock Exchange status under Australia's Foreign Investment Fund (FIF) taxation rules and Designated Investment Exchange status by the UK's Financial Services Authority.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Four banks operate in Bermuda,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> having consolidated total assets of $24.3 billion (March 2014).<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BDA_Bermuda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/BDA_Bermuda.jpg/220px-BDA_Bermuda.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/BDA_Bermuda.jpg/330px-BDA_Bermuda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/BDA_Bermuda.jpg/440px-BDA_Bermuda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2060" data-file-height="1367" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BDA_Bermuda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of Bermuda's pink-sand beaches at Astwood Park.</div></div></div>
<p>Tourism is Bermuda's second-largest industry, with the island attracting over half a million visitors annually, of whom more than 80% are from the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Other significant sources of visitors are from Canada and the United Kingdom. Tourists arrive either by cruise ship or by air at <a href="/wiki/L.F._Wade_International_Airport" title="L.F. Wade International Airport">L.F. Wade International Airport</a>, the only airport on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> However, the sector is vulnerable to external shocks, such as the 2008 recession.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_1-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The affordability of housing became a prominent issue during Bermuda's business peak in 2005 but has softened with the decline of Bermuda's real estate prices. The <a href="/wiki/World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="World Factbook">World Factbook</a> lists the average cost of a house in June 2003 as $976,000,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> while real estate agencies have claimed that this figure had risen to between $1.6 million<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> and $1.845 million by 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> though such high figures have been disputed.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Bermuda" title="List of schools in Bermuda">List of schools in Bermuda</a></div>
<p>The Bermuda Education Act 1996 requires that only three categories of schools can operate in the Bermuda Education system:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<ul><li>An <i>aided school</i> has all or a part of its property vested in a body of trustees or board of governors and is partially maintained by public funding or, since 1965 and the <a href="/wiki/Desegregation" class="mw-redirect" title="Desegregation">desegregation</a> of schools, has received a grant-in-aid out of public funds.</li>
<li>A <i>maintained school</i> has the whole of its property belonging to the Government and is fully maintained by public funds.</li>
<li>A <i>private school</i>, not maintained by public funds and which has not, since 1965 and the desegregation of schools, received any capital grant-in-aid out of public funds. The private school sector consists of six traditional private schools, two of which are religious schools, and the remaining four are secular with one of these being a single-gender school and another a <a href="/wiki/Montessori_method" class="mw-redirect" title="Montessori method">Montessori school</a>. Also, within the private sector there are a number of home schools, which must be registered with the government and receive minimal government regulation. The only boys' school opened its doors to girls in the 1990s, and in 1996, one of the aided schools became a private school.</li></ul>
<p>Prior to 1965, the Bermuda school system was racially segregated.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> When the desegregation of schools was enacted in 1965, two of the formerly maintained "white" schools and both single-sex schools opted to become private schools. The rest became part of the public school system and were either aided or maintained.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>There are 38 schools in the Bermuda Public School System, including 10 preschools, 18 primary schools, 5 middle schools, 2 senior schools (<a href="/wiki/The_Berkeley_Institute" title="The Berkeley Institute">The Berkeley Institute</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cedarbridge_Academy" title="Cedarbridge Academy">Cedarbridge Academy</a>), 1 school for students with physical and cognitive challenges, and 1 for students with behavioral problems.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> There is one aided primary school, two aided middle schools, and one aided senior school. Portuguese is taught as an optional foreign language in the Bermudian school system.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>For higher education, the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_College" title="Bermuda College">Bermuda College</a> offers various <a href="/wiki/Associate_degrees" class="mw-redirect" title="Associate degrees">associate degrees</a> and other certificate programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Bermuda does not have any four-year colleges or universities. Bermuda's graduates usually attend four-year universities in the United States, Canada and the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2009, Bermudian Government's application was approved to become a contributory member of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a> (UWI). Bermuda's membership enabled Bermudian students to enter the university at an agreed-upon subsidised rate by 2010. UWI also agreed that its Open Campus (online degree courses) would become open to Bermudian students in the future, with Bermuda becoming the 13th country to have access to the Open Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bermuda" title="Culture of Bermuda">Culture of Bermuda</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Holidays_in_Bermuda" class="mw-redirect" title="Holidays in Bermuda">Holidays in Bermuda</a></div>
