<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Bermuda%22">"Bermuda"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Bermuda%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Bermuda%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Bermuda%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Bermuda%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Bermuda%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2012</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Bermuda's culture is a mixture of the various sources of its population: Native American, Spanish-Caribbean, English, Irish, and Scots cultures were evident in the 17th century, and became part of the dominant British culture. English is the primary and official language. Due to 160 years of immigration from Portuguese Atlantic islands (primarily the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, though also from <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Verde Islands">Cape Verde Islands</a>), a portion of the population also speaks Portuguese. There are strong British influences, together with <a href="/wiki/African_diaspora" title="African diaspora">Afro-Caribbean</a> ones.
</p><p>A second wave of immigration from the West Indies was sustained throughout the 20th century; the more recent arrivals have primarily come from English-speaking countries, also bringing aspects of their cultures. This new infusion of West Indians has both accelerated social and political change, and diversified Bermuda's culture.
</p><p>The first notable, and historically important, book credited to a Bermudian was <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_Prince#Publication_of_The_History_of_Mary_Prince" title="Mary Prince">The History of Mary Prince</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Slave_narrative" title="Slave narrative">slave narrative</a> by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Prince" title="Mary Prince">Mary Prince</a>. It is thought to have contributed to the abolition of slavery in the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. <a href="/wiki/Graham_Ingham" title="Graham Ingham">Ernest Graham Ingham</a>, an expatriate author, published his books at the turn of the 19th and 20th centuries. In the 20th century, numerous books were written and published locally, though few were directed at a wider market than Bermuda. (The latter consisted primarily of scholarly works rather than creative writing). The novelist <a href="/wiki/Brian_Burland" title="Brian Burland">Brian Burland</a> (1931– 2010) achieved a degree of success and acclaim internationally. More recently, <a href="/wiki/Angela_Barry" title="Angela Barry">Angela Barry</a> has won critical recognition for her published fiction.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bermuda" title="Music of Bermuda">Music of Bermuda</a></div>
<p>Music and dance are an important part of Bermudian culture. West Indian musicians introduced <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso music</a> when Bermuda's tourist industry was expanded with the increase of visitors brought by post-Second World War aviation. Local icons, <a href="/wiki/The_Talbot_Brothers_of_Bermuda" title="The Talbot Brothers of Bermuda">The Talbot Brothers</a>, performed calypso music for many decades both in Bermuda and the United States, and appeared on the <i><a href="/wiki/Ed_Sullivan_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Ed Sullivan Show">Ed Sullivan Show</a></i>. While calypso appealed more to tourists than to the local residents, <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> has been embraced by many Bermudians since the 1970s with the influx of <a href="/wiki/Jamaicans" title="Jamaicans">Jamaican</a> immigrants.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gombey_dancers_from_Bermuda2001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Gombey_dancers_from_Bermuda2001.jpg/220px-Gombey_dancers_from_Bermuda2001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Gombey_dancers_from_Bermuda2001.jpg/330px-Gombey_dancers_from_Bermuda2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Gombey_dancers_from_Bermuda2001.jpg/440px-Gombey_dancers_from_Bermuda2001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3750" data-file-height="2460" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gombey_dancers_from_Bermuda2001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gombey dancers from Bermuda at the 2001 Smithsonian Folklife Festival in Washington, D.C.</div></div></div>
<p>Noted Bermudian musicians include <a href="/wiki/Tenor" title="Tenor">operatic tenor</a> Dr. Gary Burgess; jazz pianist <a href="/wiki/Lance_Hayward" title="Lance Hayward">Lance Hayward</a>; singer-songwriter and poet, <a href="/wiki/Heather_Nova" title="Heather Nova">Heather Nova</a>, and her brother <a href="/wiki/Mishka_(musician)" title="Mishka (musician)">Mishka</a>, reggae musician; classical musician and conductor <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Amis" title="Kenneth Amis">Kenneth Amis</a>; and more recently, <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Collie_Buddz" title="Collie Buddz">Collie Buddz</a>.
</p><p>The dances of the colourful <a href="/wiki/Gombey" title="Gombey">Gombey</a> dancers, seen at many events, are strongly influenced by African, Caribbean, Native American and British cultural traditions. In summer 2001, they performed at the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Folklife_Festival" title="Smithsonian Folklife Festival">Smithsonian Folklife Festival</a> on the <a href="/wiki/National_Mall" title="National Mall">National Mall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, United States. These Gombey Dancers continue to showcase their work for locals and visitors during the Harbour Nights festival on Bermuda's Front Street every Wednesday evening (during the summer months) and draw very large crowds.
</p><p>Bermuda's early literature was limited to the works of non-Bermudian writers commenting on the islands. These included <a href="/wiki/John_Smith_(explorer)" title="John Smith (explorer)">John Smith's</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Generall_Historie_of_Virginia,_New-England,_and_the_Summer_Isles" title="The Generall Historie of Virginia, New-England, and the Summer Isles">The Generall Historie of Virginia, New-England, and the Summer Isles</a></i> (1624), and <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Waller" title="Edmund Waller">Edmund Waller</a>'s poem, "Battle of the Summer Islands" (1645).<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bermuda is the only place name in the New World that is alluded to in the works of <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a>; it is mentioned in his play <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tempest" title="The Tempest">The Tempest</a></i>, in Act 1, Scene 2, line 230: "the still-vexed Bermoothes", this being a reference to the Bermudas.
</p><p>Local artwork may be viewed at several galleries around Bermuda, and watercolours painted by local artists are also on sale. Alfred Birdsey was one of the more famous and talented watercolourists; his impressionistic landscapes of <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Bermuda" title="Hamilton, Bermuda">Hamilton</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Bermuda" title="St. George&#39;s, Bermuda">St George's</a>, and the surrounding sailboats, homes, and bays of Bermuda, are world-renowned. Hand-carved cedar sculptures are another speciality. One such 7&#160;ft (2.1&#160;m) sculpture, created by Bermudian sculptor Chesley Trott, is installed at the airport's baggage claim area. In 2010, his sculpture <i>We Arrive</i> was unveiled in Barr's Bay Park, overlooking <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Harbour,_Bermuda" title="Hamilton Harbour, Bermuda">Hamilton Harbour</a>, to commemorate the freeing of slaves in 1835 from the American brig <i><a href="/wiki/Enterprise_(slave_ship)" title="Enterprise (slave ship)">Enterprise</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Local resident Tom Butterfield founded the <a href="/wiki/Masterworks_Museum_of_Bermuda_Art" title="Masterworks Museum of Bermuda Art">Masterworks Museum of Bermuda Art</a> in 1986, initially featuring works about Bermuda by artists from other countries. He began with pieces by American artists, such as <a href="/wiki/Winslow_Homer" title="Winslow Homer">Winslow Homer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Demuth" title="Charles Demuth">Charles Demuth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_O%27Keeffe" title="Georgia O&#39;Keeffe">Georgia O'Keeffe</a>, who had lived and worked on Bermuda. He has increasingly supported the development of local artists, arts education, and the arts scene.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, the museum opened its new building, constructed within the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Botanical_Gardens" title="Bermuda Botanical Gardens">Botanical Gardens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bermuda hosts an annual international film festival, which shows many independent films. One of the founders is film producer and director <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Rankin,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Arthur Rankin, Jr.">Arthur Rankin, Jr.</a>, co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/Rankin/Bass" class="mw-redirect" title="Rankin/Bass">Rankin/Bass</a> production company.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bermudian model <a href="/wiki/Gina_Swainson" title="Gina Swainson">Gina Swainson</a> was crowned "<a href="/wiki/Miss_World" title="Miss World">Miss World</a>" in 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_and_recreation_in_Bermuda" title="Sports and recreation in Bermuda">Sports and recreation in Bermuda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:95_Coy_RGA_team_and_Governor%27s_Cup_in_Bermuda_1917.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/95_Coy_RGA_team_and_Governor%27s_Cup_in_Bermuda_1917.jpg/220px-95_Coy_RGA_team_and_Governor%27s_Cup_in_Bermuda_1917.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/95_Coy_RGA_team_and_Governor%27s_Cup_in_Bermuda_1917.jpg/330px-95_Coy_RGA_team_and_Governor%27s_Cup_in_Bermuda_1917.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/95_Coy_RGA_team_and_Governor%27s_Cup_in_Bermuda_1917.jpg/440px-95_Coy_RGA_team_and_Governor%27s_Cup_in_Bermuda_1917.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5815" data-file-height="3131" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:95_Coy_RGA_team_and_Governor%27s_Cup_in_Bermuda_1917.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The football team of 95 Company, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Garrison_Artillery" title="Royal Garrison Artillery">Royal Garrison Artillery</a>, victors in the 1917 Governor's Cup football match, pose with the cup. The cup was contested for annually by teams from annually by teams from the various Royal Navy, British Army <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Garrison" title="Bermuda Garrison">Bermuda Garrison</a>, and Royal Air Force units stationed in Bermuda.</div></div></div>
<p>Many sports popular today were formalised by British <a href="/wiki/Public_school_(United_Kingdom)" title="Public school (United Kingdom)">Public schools</a> and universities in the 19th century. These schools produced the civil servants and military and naval officers required to build and maintain the <a href="/wiki/British_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="British empire">British empire</a>, and team sports were considered a vital tool for training their students to think and act as part of a team. Former public schoolboys continued to pursue these activities, and founded organisations such as <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">the Football Association</a> (FA). Today's association of football with the working classes began in 1885 when the FA changed its rules to allow professional players.
</p><p>The professionals soon displaced the amateur ex-Public schoolboys. Bermuda's role as the primary Royal Navy base in the Western Hemisphere, with an army garrison to match, ensured that the naval and military officers quickly introduced the newly formalised sports to Bermuda, including <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby football</a>, and even <a href="/wiki/Lawn_tennis" class="mw-redirect" title="Lawn tennis">tennis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a> (rowing did not adapt well from British rivers to the stormy Atlantic. The officers soon switched to <a href="/wiki/Yacht_racing" title="Yacht racing">sail racing</a>, founding the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bermuda_Yacht_Club" title="Royal Bermuda Yacht Club">Royal Bermuda Yacht Club</a>). Once these sports reached Bermuda, they were eagerly adopted by Bermudians.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bermuda_national_cricket_team" title="Bermuda national cricket team">Bermuda's national cricket team</a> participated in the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup_2007" class="mw-redirect" title="Cricket World Cup 2007">Cricket World Cup 2007</a> in the West Indies. Their most famous player is a 130 kilograms (290&#160;lb) police officer named <a href="/wiki/Dwayne_Leverock" title="Dwayne Leverock">Dwayne Leverock</a>. But India defeated Bermuda and set a record of 413 runs in a <a href="/wiki/One-Day_International" class="mw-redirect" title="One-Day International">One-Day International</a> (ODI). Bermuda were knocked out of the World Cup. Also very well known is <a href="/wiki/David_Hemp" title="David Hemp">David Hemp</a>, a former captain of <a href="/wiki/Glamorgan_County_Cricket_Club" title="Glamorgan County Cricket Club">Glamorgan</a> in <a href="/wiki/List_of_current_first-class_cricket_teams#England_and_Wales" title="List of current first-class cricket teams">English first class cricket</a>. The annual "Cup Match" cricket tournament between rival parishes St George's in the east and Somerset in the west is the occasion for a popular national holiday. This tournament began in 1872 when Captain Moresby of the Royal Navy introduced the game to Bermuda, holding a match at Somerset to mark <i>forty years since the unjust thraldom of slavery</i>. The East End versus West End rivalry resulted from the locations of the <i>St. George's Garrison</i> (the original army headquarters in Bermuda) on Barrack Hill, St. George's, and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Dockyard,_Bermuda" title="Royal Naval Dockyard, Bermuda">Royal Naval Dockyard</a> at Ireland Island. Moresby founded the Somerset Cricket Club which plays the St. George's Cricket Club in this game (the membership of both clubs has long been mostly civilian).<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, Bermuda hosted the 25th <a href="/wiki/PGA_Grand_Slam_of_Golf" title="PGA Grand Slam of Golf">PGA Grand Slam of Golf</a>. This 36-hole event was held on 16–17 October 2007, at the <a href="/wiki/Mid_Ocean_Club" title="Mid Ocean Club">Mid Ocean Club</a> in Tucker's Town. This season-ending tournament is limited to four golfers: the winners of the <a href="/wiki/Masters_Tournament" title="Masters Tournament">Masters</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Open_(golf)" title="U.S. Open (golf)">U.S. Open</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Open_Championship" title="The Open Championship">British Open</a> and <a href="/wiki/PGA_Championship" title="PGA Championship">PGA Championship</a>. The event returned to Bermuda in 2008 and 2009. One-armed Bermudian golfer <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quinn_Talbot&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Quinn Talbot (page does not exist)">Quinn Talbot</a> was both the United States National Amputee Golf Champion for five successive years and the British World One-Arm Golf Champion.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:International_One_Design_-_Hamilton_Harbour_-_Bermuda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/International_One_Design_-_Hamilton_Harbour_-_Bermuda.jpg/170px-International_One_Design_-_Hamilton_Harbour_-_Bermuda.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/International_One_Design_-_Hamilton_Harbour_-_Bermuda.jpg/255px-International_One_Design_-_Hamilton_Harbour_-_Bermuda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/International_One_Design_-_Hamilton_Harbour_-_Bermuda.jpg/340px-International_One_Design_-_Hamilton_Harbour_-_Bermuda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:International_One_Design_-_Hamilton_Harbour_-_Bermuda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/International_One_Design" title="International One Design">IOD</a> racer on a mooring in <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_Harbour,_Bermuda" title="Hamilton Harbour, Bermuda">Hamilton Harbour</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The Government announced in 2006 that it would provide substantial financial support to Bermuda's cricket and <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_national_football_team" title="Bermuda national football team">football</a> teams. Football did not become popular with Bermudians 'til after the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, though teams from the various Royal Navy, British Army <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Garrison" title="Bermuda Garrison">Bermuda Garrison</a>, and Royal Air Force units of Bermuda had competed annually for the Governor's Cup introduced by Major-General Sir <a href="/wiki/George_Bullock_(British_Army_officer)" title="George Bullock (British Army officer)">George Mackworth Bullock</a> in 1913. A combined team of the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Militia_Artillery" title="Bermuda Militia Artillery">Bermuda Militia Artillery</a> (BMA) and the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Militia_Infantry" title="Bermuda Militia Infantry">Bermuda Militia Infantry</a> (BMI) defeated <a href="/wiki/HMS_Malabar_(shore_establishment)" class="mw-redirect" title="HMS Malabar (shore establishment)">HMS&#160;<i>Malabar</i></a> to win the cup on 21 March 1943, becoming the first team of a locally raised unit to do so, and the third British Army team to do so since 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Bermuda's most prominent footballers are <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Best" title="Clyde Best">Clyde Best</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Goater" title="Shaun Goater">Shaun Goater</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Lightbourne" title="Kyle Lightbourne">Kyle Lightbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Lambe" title="Reggie Lambe">Reggie Lambe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Nusum" title="Sam Nusum">Sam Nusum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nahki_Wells" title="Nahki Wells">Nahki Wells</a>. In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Hogges" class="mw-redirect" title="Bermuda Hogges">Bermuda Hogges</a> were formed as the nation's first professional football team to raise the standard of play for the Bermuda national football team. The team played in the <a href="/wiki/United_Soccer_Leagues_Second_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="United Soccer Leagues Second Division">United Soccer Leagues Second Division</a> but folded in 2013.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sailing" title="Sailing">Sailing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian</a> sports are popular with both residents and visitors alike. The prestigious <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Race" class="mw-redirect" title="Bermuda Race">Newport–Bermuda Yacht Race</a> is a more than 100-year-old tradition, with boats racing between <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport, Rhode Island</a> and Bermuda. In 2007, the 16th biennial <a href="/wiki/Marion,_Massachusetts" title="Marion, Massachusetts">Marion</a>-Bermuda yacht race occurred. A sport unique to Bermuda is racing the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Fitted_Dinghy" title="Bermuda Fitted Dinghy">Bermuda Fitted Dinghy</a>. <a href="/wiki/International_One_Design" title="International One Design">International One Design</a> racing also originated in Bermuda.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In December 2013, Bermuda's bid to host the <a href="/wiki/2017_America%27s_Cup" title="2017 America&#39;s Cup">2017 America's Cup</a> was announced.
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics" title="Bermuda at the 2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics</a>, Bermuda competed in sailing, athletics, swimming, diving, triathlon and equestrian events. In those Olympics, Bermuda's Katura Horton-Perinchief made history by becoming the first black female diver to compete in the Olympic Games. Bermuda has had one Olympic medallist, <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Hill_(boxer)" title="Clarence Hill (boxer)">Clarence Hill</a>, who won a bronze medal in boxing. Bermuda also competed in Men's <a href="/wiki/Skeleton_(sport)" title="Skeleton (sport)">Skeleton</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics" title="2006 Winter Olympics">2006 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>, Italy. Patrick Singleton placed 19th, with a final time of 1:59.81. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jillian_Teceira&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jillian Teceira (page does not exist)">Jillian Teceira</a> competed in the Beijing Olympics in 2008. It is tradition for Bermuda to march in the Opening Ceremony in <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_shorts" title="Bermuda shorts">Bermuda shorts</a>, regardless of the summer or winter Olympic celebration. Bermuda also competes in the biennial <a href="/wiki/Island_Games" title="Island Games">Island Games</a>, which it hosted in 2013.
</p><p>In 1998, Bermuda established its own Basketball Association.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Since then, its <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_national_basketball_team" title="Bermuda national basketball team">national team</a> has taken advantage of Bermuda's advanced basketball facilities<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> and competed at the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean Basketball Championship">Caribbean Basketball Championship</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bermuda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Hospitals_Board" title="Bermuda Hospitals Board">Bermuda Hospitals Board</a> operates the King Edward VII Memorial Hospital, located in <a href="/wiki/Paget_Parish" title="Paget Parish">Paget Parish</a>, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mid-Atlantic_Wellness_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mid-Atlantic Wellness Institute (page does not exist)">Mid-Atlantic Wellness Institute</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Devonshire_Parish" title="Devonshire Parish">Devonshire Parish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Boston's Lahey Medical Center has an established visiting specialists program on the island which provides Bermudians and expats with access to specialists regularly on the island.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  There were about 6,000 hospital admissions, 30,000 emergency department attendances and 6,300 outpatient procedures in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Unlike the other territories that still remain under British rule, Bermuda does not have <a href="/wiki/National_health_insurance" title="National health insurance">national healthcare</a>. Employers must provide a healthcare plan and pay for up to 50% of the cost for each employee.<sup id="cite_ref-Healthcare_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Healthcare-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Healthcare is a mandatory requirement and is expensive, even with the help provided by employers, though no more expensive than that which an employee in the US would typically pay for healthcare when obtained through their employer<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and the coverage typically far exceeds that which one may have through their employer in the US<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. There are only a few approved healthcare providers that offer insurance to Bermudians.<sup id="cite_ref-Healthcare_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Healthcare-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In 2016 these were the Bermudan government's Health Insurance Department, three other approved licensed health insurance companies, and three approved health insurance schemes (provided by the Bermudan government for its employees and by two banks).<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are no <a href="/wiki/Paramedic" title="Paramedic">paramedics</a> on the island.  The Bermuda Hospitals Board says that they were not vital in Bermuda because of its small size.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Nurse_practitioner" title="Nurse practitioner">Nurse practitioners</a> on the island, of which there are not many, can be granted authority to write prescriptions “under the authority of a medical practitioner”.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-Bermuda_2010_Census-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Bermuda_2010_Census_2-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Bermuda_2010_Census_2-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130228051323/http://unstats.un.org/unsd/demographic/sources/census/2010_phc/bermuda/Bermuda_new.pdf">"Bermuda 2010 Census"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://bermuda-online.org/bdagovt.htm">"Bermuda Government today"</a>. <i>Bermuda-Online.org</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">9 July</span> 2010</span>. <q>In July 2003, Bermuda formally joined the Caribbean Community as an Associate Member (non-voting member), in certain areas but not in others. This specifically excludes free movement of Caribbean nationals to Bermuda, and any prospect of Bermuda joining CARIFTA or its newest free trade organization; the Free Trade Area of the Americas (FTAA). Membership of the Caribbean Community costs Bermuda about US$90,000 a year. Direct trade between Bermuda and Caribbean countries is also welcomed and encouraged, especially given the close or extended family links many Bermudians have with Caribbean islands or territories.&#160;... All visitors to Bermuda who are nationals of and resident in Caribbean islands must come via the USA or Canada or United Kingdom and must have appropriate visas to come via those countries. Effective January 2003, all Jamaican nationals who are not Bermudian must also have a visa to enter Bermuda on business or vacation.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Bermuda-Online.org&amp;rft.atitle=Bermuda+Government+today&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbermuda-online.org%2Fbdagovt.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABermuda" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li><span style="font-size:85%;"><sup>2</sup> <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British overseas territory</a> awaiting entrustment to join the CSME</span></li></ul>
</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
